Amm and Khass — General and Specific

When a Companion Specifies a General Text: The Apostate Woman
Dispute on specifying a general hadith using a Companion's opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi principle that a Companion's opinion can specify an amm text and evaluate the Shafi'i objection based on the prohibition of abandoning the general.

Core Idea
A Companion's interpretation can specify a general hadith, but the Shafi'i school rejects this as abandoning the text.

This passage pits two usul principles against each other: the generality of a textual command versus the interpretive authority of a Companion who was present when the text was revealed. The hadith 'Who changes his religion, kill him' appears unconditional, yet Ibn Abbas – a Companion and the very narrator of the hadith – exempts apostate women. Al-Shafi'i argues that we cannot set aside the general command based on a Companion's opinion. The Hanafi school, however, considers Ibn Abbas's statement as evidence that the hadith was never intended to be general in the first place, or that specification is valid. Let's dissect this foundational usul dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Text
Locate the hadith cited: 'Who changes his religion, kill him.' Recognize it as an amm (general) command that linguistically includes any person who apostatizes.
This hadith is narrated by Ibn Abbas himself, which is significant.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Ibn Abbas's statement: 'The apostate woman is not killed but imprisoned and compelled to Islam.' This is transmitted via Abu Hanifa. The Hanafi school relies on this as a specification (takhsis) of the general hadith.
The chain includes Abu Hanifa, making it a key Hanafi proof.
3
State the Shafi'i Objection
Al-Shafi'i argues that refraining from acting on a general text is the same as acting against it, which is prohibited. Therefore, a mere Companion opinion cannot override the generality.
This reflects the Shafi'i usul that amm is zanni and can be specified only by another text or consensus.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The footnote questions: if the hadith is truly general (mufid al-umum), how could Ibn Abbas contradict it? The Hanafi answer is that the Companion's understanding reveals that the hadith was not general from the outset, or that specification is permissible through his qawl.
Hanafi usul holds that a Companion's fatwa can specify an amm if it does not contradict a clear text, because Companions had direct knowledge of the revelation's context.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis rule that an apostate woman is not killed but imprisoned and compelled to Islam. Shafi'is rule that she is killed like a male apostate.
This difference flows from the usul principle, not from a different ruling on apostasy itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فاقتلوه ذلك حديث عبد الله بن عباس رضي الله عنهما : «مَن بدل دينه : وقال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : لا تُقتل المرتدة . وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : لا يُترَك عموم الحديث بقوله وتخصيصه، والامتناع عن العمل به مثل العمل بخلافه؛ لأن الامتناع حرام، مثل العمل بخلافه، والله أعلم. حديث ابن عباس عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن بدل دينه فاقتلوه لفظ ابن ماجه وأخرجه البخاري وبقية أصحاب السنن في قصة. قوله : وقال ابن عباس: لا تُقتل المرتدة أخرج ابن أبي شيبة حدثنا عبد الرحيم بن سليمان ووكيع عن أبي حنيفة عن عاصم عن أبي رزين عن ابن عباس قال: لا تقتل النساء إذا ارتددن عن الإسلام، ولكن يُحبسن ويُدعَين إلى الإسلام، ويُجبرن عليه»، وأخرجه الدارقطني من طريق أبي مالك النخعي عن عاصم قلت: وقد قالوا: محلَّ هذا : إذا لم يكن المرفوع عاماً، وهذا المرفوع عام، فأَنَّى يستقيم؟ والله أعلم.
And from [the chapter] 'kill him': that is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both: 'Who changes his religion, kill him.' And Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: 'The apostate woman is not killed.' And Al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'The generality of the hadith is not abandoned by his statement and its specification, and refraining from acting upon it is like acting contrary to it; because refraining is prohibited, just like acting contrary to it.' And Allah knows best. Hadith of Ibn Abbas: from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, said: 'Who changes his religion, kill him' – wording of Ibn Majah, and it was also recorded by Al-Bukhari and the rest of the authors of the Sunan in a story. His statement: 'And Ibn Abbas said: The apostate woman is not killed' – Ibn Abi Shaybah recorded: 'Abd al-Rahim ibn Sulayman and Waki' narrated to us from Abu Hanifah from 'Asim from Abu Razin from Ibn Abbas who said: Women are not to be killed when they apostatize from Islam, but they are to be imprisoned, called to Islam, and compelled to it.' And Al-Daraqutni recorded it via Abu Malik al-Nakha'i from 'Asim. I said: And they said: The place of this is when the raised [hadith] is not general, but this raised [hadith] is general, so how can it be correct? And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage presents a usul dispute regarding the application of a general (amm) hadith. The text begins by citing the famous hadith reported by Ibn Abbas: 'Who changes his religion, kill him.' This is a general command. However, Ibn Abbas himself is reported to have said that the apostate woman is not killed but is imprisoned and compelled to return to Islam. This creates an apparent contradiction: a Companion (Ibn Abbas) appears to restrict the generality of the hadith. Al-Shafi'i argues that one cannot abandon the generality of the hadith merely because of Ibn Abbas's statement, because refraining from acting on the hadith is equivalent to acting contrary to it, and both are prohibited. The footnote then provides the chain of transmission for Ibn Abbas's statement and questions how Ibn Abbas could restrict a general hadith. The passage does not resolve the dispute but lays out the positions.

Key Terms
العموم (al-umum): A word that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
المرتدة (al-murtaddah): A woman who apostatizes from Islam.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term to exclude some of its individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the key point of disagreement between Ibn Abbas (and the Hanafis) and Al-Shafi'i in this passage?
A) Whether the hadith 'Who changes his religion, kill him' is authentic.
B) Whether the hadith applies to apostate women.
C) Whether apostasy is punished by death.
D) Whether a woman can be imprisoned.

Key Takeaway
A Companion's opinion can specify a general text in Hanafi usul, but Shafi'i usul requires stronger evidence to abandon the general; this difference produces a concrete fiqh difference on the treatment of apostate women.

Understanding Contradiction (Mu'arada) in Usul: Definition, Conditions, and Resolution
Definition and resolution of contradiction (mu'arada).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define mu'arada, identify its pillar and condition, and apply the Hanafi resolution hierarchy to cases of contradictory evidences.

Core Idea
Contradiction among texts is resolved by seeking abrogation; contradiction among qiyas allows the mujtahid's choice.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul sets the framework for handling apparent contradictions between legal proofs. It defines the concept of mu'arada, its essential elements (pillar and condition), and outlines a step-by-step hierarchy for resolution, emphasizing the critical distinction between contradictions involving textual sources (Book and Sunnah) and those involving analogical reasoning (qiyas).

Guided Path
1
Define mu'arada
Identify the linguistic and technical meaning of mu'arada from the text: 'mutual prevention in the manner of confrontation' and 'equal opposition of two proofs in two opposing rulings'.
Linguistic root: 'arada (to present, obstruct).
2
Identify the pillar (rukn)
The pillar is the equal confrontation of two proofs with no advantage for either, regarding two contradictory rulings. The pillar is what the concept stands upon.
Rukn al-mu'arada: تقابل الحجتين على السواء.
3
Identify the condition (shart)
The condition is unity of subject (mahall) and time (waqt) along with opposite rulings (e.g., halal and haram). If subject or time differ, it is not true contradiction.
Example: marriage causes permissibility for one subject and prohibition for another.
4
Outline the resolution hierarchy for texts
For two verses: recourse to Sunnah. For two Sunnahs or a Sunnah and a verse: recourse to qiyas, then Companion statements, in order of evidence. This is because ignorance of abrogation blocks acting on both.
Abrogation is possible only in textual sources.
5
Distinguish the case of qiyas contradiction
When two qiyas contradict, they do not fall; the mujtahid may act by whichever he wishes by his inner conviction (shahadat al-qalb). This is because qiyas is based on opinion and cannot abrogate.
The truth in ijtihad is one but the mujtahid is rewarded even if mistaken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المعارضة
وإذا ثبت أن التعارض ليس بأصل: كان الأصل في الباب: طلب ما يدفع التعارض، وإذا جاء العجز وجب إثبات حكم التعارض.
وهذا الفصل أربعة أقسام في الأصل:
وهو معرفة التعارض لغةً، وشرطه، وركنه، وحكمه شريعة. أما معنى المعارضة لغةً: فالممانعة على سبيل المقابلة، يقال: عَرَضَ لي كذا: أي استقبلني بصد، ومنع وسميت الموانع عوارض. وركن المعارضة: تقابل الحجتين على السواء، لا مزية لإحداهما، في حكمين متضادين. فركنُ كل شيء ما يقوم به.
وأما الشرط: فاتحاد المحل والوقت، مع تضاد الحكم، مثل التحليل والتحريم، وذلك لأن التضادَّ لا يقع في محلين؛ لجواز اجتماعهما، مثل النكاح: يوجب الحل في محل والحرمة في غيره وكذلك في وقتين؛ لجواز اجتماعهما في محل واحد، في وقتين مثل حرمة الخمر بعد حلها.
وحكم المعارضة بين آيتين: المصير إلى السنة. وبين السنتين نوعان: المصير إلى القياس وأقوال الصحابة رضي الله عنهم على الترتيب في الحجج إن أمكن؛ لأن الجهل بالناسخ: يمنع العمل بهما. وعند العجز: يجب تقرير الأصول. وإذا ثبت أن الأصل في وقوع المعارضة الجهل بالناسخ والمنسوخ ذلك بالكتاب والسنة فكان بين آيتين أو قراءتين في آية، أو بين سنتين، أو سنة وآية؛ لأن النسخ في ذلك كله سائغ، على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما بين قياسين، أو قولي الصحابة رضي الله عنهم: فلا؛ لأن القياس لا يصلح ناسخاً، وقول الصحابي بناءً على رأيه، فحل محل القياس أيضاً. وبيان ذلك أن القياسين إذا تعارضا لم يسقطا بالتعارض ليجب العمل بهما بالحال بل يعمل المجتهد بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه؛ لأن تعارض النصين كان لجهلنا بالناسخ من المنسوخ، والجهل لا يصلح دليلاً شرعياً لحكم شرعي، وهو الاختيار. وأما تعارض القياسين: فلم يقع من قبل الجهل من كل وجه؛ لأن ذلك وضعُ الشرع في حق العمل، فأما في الحقيقة: فلا، من قبل أن الحق في المجتهدات واحدٌ يُصيبه المجتهد مرةً، ويُخطئ أخرى، إلا أنه لما كان مأجوراً على عمله وجب التخيير؛ لاعتبار شبهة الحقية في حق نفس العمل، ووجب العمل بشهادة القلب؛ لأنه دليل عند الضرورة؛ لاختصاص القلب بنور الفراسة. وأما فيما يحتمل النسخ: فجهل محض بلا شبهة، ولأن القول بتعارض القياسين يوجب العمل بلا دليل وهو الحال، وتعارض الحجتين من الكتاب والسنة يوجب العمل بالقياس الذي هو حجة. ومثال ذلك: أن المسافر إذا كان معه إناءان في أحدهما ماء نجس،
Chapter on Contradiction. If it is established that contradiction is not a principle, then the principle in this chapter is to seek what removes contradiction, and if inability arises, it is necessary to establish the ruling of contradiction. This section has four divisions in principle: knowing the meaning of contradiction linguistically, its condition, its pillar, and its ruling in Sharia. As for the meaning of mu'arada linguistically: it is prevention in the manner of confrontation. It is said: 'such and such presented to me' meaning it faced me with prevention, and obstacles are called 'awarid. The pillar of mu'arada: the confrontation of two proofs equally, with no advantage for one over the other, regarding two opposing rulings. For the pillar of everything is that by which it stands. As for the condition: unity of subject and time, along with opposition of ruling, like permissibility and prohibition. This is because opposition does not occur in two subjects due to the possibility of their coexistence, such as marriage: it necessitates permissibility in one subject and prohibition in another. Similarly in two times, due to the possibility of their coexistence in one subject at two times, like the prohibition of wine after its permissibility. The ruling of contradiction between two verses: recourse to the Sunnah. And between two Sunnahs: two types: recourse to qiyas and the statements of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) in order of evidence if possible; because ignorance of the abrogator prevents acting upon both. And when unable, it is necessary to establish the principles. And if it is established that the origin in the occurrence of contradiction is ignorance of the abrogating and abrogated, that is by the Book and Sunnah, then it is between two verses or two readings in a verse, or between two Sunnahs, or a Sunnah and a verse; because abrogation is permissible in all of that, as we will explain if Allah wills. As for between two qiyas or two statements of the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them): no, because qiyas is not valid as an abrogator, and the statement of a Companion is based on his opinion, so it takes the place of qiyas as well. Explanation: when two qiyas contradict, they do not fall due to contradiction, requiring one to act upon them immediately; rather, the mujtahid acts with whichever he wishes by his inner conviction. Because the contradiction of two texts was due to our ignorance of the abrogator from the abrogated, and ignorance is not a valid legal evidence for a legal ruling, and that is the chosen view. As for contradiction of two qiyas: it does not occur due to ignorance in every respect, because that is the law's position regarding practice. As for in reality, no, because the truth in matters of ijtihad is one; the mujtahid hits it sometimes and misses another, but since he is rewarded for his action, choice is necessary due to considering the semblance of truth regarding the act itself, and it is necessary to act by inner conviction because it is evidence in necessity, due to the heart being endowed with insight. As for what is subject to abrogation: it is pure ignorance without semblance. And because the statement of contradiction of two qiyas requires action without evidence, which is the state, while the contradiction of two proofs from the Book and Sunnah requires action by qiyas, which is evidence. An example: a traveler who has two containers, in one of which is impure water.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage is from al-Bazdawi's Usul, beginning the chapter on contradiction (mu'arada). The author first establishes that contradiction is not the default principle; rather, the aim is to resolve it. He then outlines four aspects of contradiction: its linguistic definition, pillar, condition, and ruling. Linguistically, mu'arada means mutual prevention with confrontation. The pillar of contradiction is the equal opposition of two proofs regarding two contradictory rulings. The condition is unity of subject and time, along with opposite rulings (e.g., halal vs. haram). If the subject or time differ, it is not true contradiction. For the ruling, the text explains the hierarchy: contradiction between two Quranic verses is resolved by resorting to the Sunnah. Between two Sunnahs, one turns to qiyas and then to Companion statements, in order of evidence strength. This is because the contradiction indicates ignorance of abrogation, which blocks acting on both. If still unable to resolve, one must fall back on the established principles (usul). The author distinguishes between contradictions among texts (which admit abrogation) and contradictions among qiyas or Companion statements (which do not). Qiyas cannot abrogate; it is based on opinion. When two qiyas conflict, the mujtahid may choose whichever his heart prefers, since the truth in ijtihad matters is one but the mujtahid may err; however, he is rewarded in either case. Acting by inner conviction is permitted due to necessity. This contrasts with textual contradiction, where ignorance of abrogation is absolute, requiring resolution via other evidence. The example of a traveler with two containers, one with impure water, illustrates the practical difficulty.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'āraḍah): Mutual opposition of two proofs equally, in two contradictory rulings, on the same subject and time.
ركن المعارضة (rukn al-mu'āraḍah): The confrontation of two proofs on equal footing without advantage, in two opposing rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of contradiction between two qiyas according to the Hanafi school?
A) They both become invalid, and one must seek a third evidence.
B) The mujtahid may act by whichever he chooses based on his inner conviction.
C) One must prefer the qiyas that agrees with the Quran.
D) The contradiction indicates abrogation, so one must find the abrogator.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi resolution of contradiction distinguishes between textual evidence (where abrogation is sought) and analogical reasoning (where the mujtahid may choose by inner conviction).

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Conflict of Evidence: Naskh vs. Qiyas
Explaining when conflict indicates naskh and when it does not.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between conflict of textual evidences (naskh) and conflict of analogical deductions (qiyas), and apply the Hanafi rule of shahadat al-qalb.

Core Idea
The heart's testimony is a valid proof when analogies conflict; the mujtahid chooses by intuitive conviction.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh addresses a fundamental question: how should a mujtahid proceed when two pieces of evidence appear to conflict? The answer depends on whether the conflict involves primary texts (Quran and Sunnah) or secondary proofs such as analogical reasoning (qiyas) and Companion statements. For texts, the underlying cause is ignorance of abrogation; for analogies, the Law itself has placed ijtihad as a basis for action, allowing the mujtahid to rely on the testimony of his heart.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of conflict
Read the passage and locate the distinction: conflict between textual evidences (verses, hadiths) and conflict between analogies or Companion statements.
Textual conflict is attributed to ignorance of naskh; analogical conflict is not.
2
Understand the cause of each conflict
For texts, the cause is our ignorance of which text abrogates which. For analogies, the cause is not ignorance but the nature of ijtihad—truth is one but the mujtahid may miss it.
Ignorance cannot serve as a proof; hence texts require naskh. For qiyas, action is still possible.
3
Recognize the resolution for each
Textual conflict: must seek abrogating and abrogated. Analogical conflict: the mujtahid may choose any of the conflicting analogies by testimony of his heart (shahadat al-qalb).
Shahadat al-qalb is a valid proof in cases of necessity (darura).
4
Apply the examples from the passage
Examine the examples: traveler with water containers (tayammum) vs. garments (taharri) vs. ambiguous qibla (taharri). Understand why shahadat al-qalb is allowed in some cases but not others.
Key: darura (necessity) triggers shahadat al-qalb; mere inability (ajz) does not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند العجز : يجب تقرير الأصول. وإذا ثبت أن الأصل في وقوع المعارضة الجهل بالناسخ والمنسوخ ذلك بالكتاب والسنة فكان بين آيتين أو قراءتين في آية، أو بين سنتين، أو سنةٍ وآية ؛ لأن النسخ في ذلك كله سائغ، على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى. وأما بين قياسين، أو قولي الصحابة رضي الله عنهم : فلا؛ لأن القياس لا يصلح ناسخاً، وقول الصحابي بناءً على رأيه، فحل محل القياس أيضاً. وبيان ذلك أن القياسين إذا تعارضا لم يسقطا بالتعارض ليجب العمل به بالحال بل يعمل المجتهد بأيهما شاء بشهادة قلبه ؛ لأن تعارض النصين كان لجهلنا بالناسخ من المنسوخ، والجهل لا يصلح دليلاً شرعياً لحكم شرعي، وهو الاختيار. وأما تعارض القياسين : فلم يقع من قبل الجهل من كل وجه؛ لأن ذلك وضعُ الشرع في حق العمل، فأما في الحقيقة: فلا، من قبل أن الحق في المجتهدات واحدٌ يُصيبه المجتهد مرةً، ويُخطئ أخرى، إلا أنه لما كان مأجوراً على عمله وجب التخيير ؛ لاعتبار شبهة الحقية في حق نفس العمل، ووجب العمل بشهادة القلب؛ لأنه دليل عند الضرورة؛ لاختصاص القلب بنور الفراسة. وأما فيما يحتمل النسخ: فجهل محض بلا شبهة، ولأن القول بتعارض القياسين يوجب العمل بلا دليل وهو الحال، وتعارض الحجتين من الكتاب والسنة يوجب العمل بالقياس الذي هو حجة. ومثال ذلك : أن المسافر إذا كان معه إناءان في أحدهما ماء نجس، والآخر طاهر، وهو لا يدري: عمل بالتيمم؛ لأنه طهور مطلق عند العجز، وقد وقع العجزُ بالتعارض فلم تقع الضرورة، فلم يجز العمل بشهادة القلب. ولو كان معه ثوبان نجس وطاهر، ولا ثوبَ غيرهما : عمل بالتحري؛ لضرورة الوقوع في العمل بلا دليل، وهو الحال. وكذلك من اشتبهت عليه القبلة ولا دليل معه أصلاً عمل بشهادة قلبه من غير مجرد الاختيار ؛ لما قلنا إن الصواب واحد منهما، فلم يسقط الابتلاء، بل وجب العمل بشهادة قلبه. وإذا عمل بذلك : لم يجز نقضه إلا بدليل فوقه يوجب نقض الأول، حتى لم يجز نقض حكم أمضي بالاجتهاد بمثله؛ لأن الأول ترجح بالعمل به ولم يُنقض التحري باليقين في القبلة؛ لأن اليقين حادث ليس بمناقض، بمنزلة نص نزل بخلاف الاجتهاد، أو إجماع انعقد بعد إمضاء حكم الاجتهاد على خلافه. وأما العمل به في المستقبل على خلاف الأول : فنوعان : إن كان الحكم المطلوب به يَحتمل الانتقال: وجب العمل به، وإلا : فلا، وبيانُه : أن المتحري في القبلة إذا تبدل تحريه : عَمِلَ به في المستقبل ؛ لأن حكم القبلة يحتمل الانتقال من جهة إلى جهة، حتى إنه انتقل من بيت المقدس إلى الكعبة وانتقل من عين الكعبة إلى جهتها، فصلح التحري دليلاً على خلاف الأول، وكذلك في سائر المجتهدات في المشروعات القابلة للانتقال والتعاقب. وأما الذي لا يحتمله: فرجلٌ صلى في ثوب على تحري طهارته حقيقةً
And when unable, the principles must be established. And if it is established that the origin of conflict is ignorance of the abrogating and abrogated in the Book and Sunnah, so it is between two verses or two readings in a verse, or between two sunnahs, or a sunnah and a verse; because abrogation in all that is permissible, as we will explain if God wills. As for between two analogies, or two statements of the Companions (may God be pleased with them): no; because analogy is not valid as an abrogator, and the statement of a Companion is based on his opinion, so it takes the place of analogy as well. Explanation: when two analogies conflict, they are not dropped by conflict so that one must act by one of them immediately. Rather, the mujtahid acts with whichever he wishes by testimony of his heart; because conflict between two texts was due to our ignorance of the abrogating from the abrogated, and ignorance is not a valid legal proof for a legal ruling, and that is the choice. As for conflict of two analogies: it did not occur from the side of ignorance in every respect; because that is the placement of the Law in respect of action. As for in reality: no, because the truth in matters of ijtihad is one; the mujtahid hits it sometimes and misses another, except that since he is rewarded for his action, choice is obligatory to consider the semblance of truth in respect of the action itself, and action by testimony of the heart is obligatory because it is a proof in necessity; due to the heart's being distinguished with the light of insight. As for what admits abrogation: it is pure ignorance without semblance, and because saying two analogies conflict necessitates acting without proof, and that is the case; and conflict of two proofs from the Book and Sunnah necessitates acting by analogy which is a proof. Example: a traveler, if he has two containers, one containing impure water and the other pure, and he does not know: he performs tayammum; because it is absolute purifier when unable, and inability has occurred by conflict, so necessity did not occur, so acting by testimony of the heart is not permissible. And if he had two garments, impure and pure, and no garment other than them: he acts by conjecture due to the necessity of falling into action without proof, and that is the case. Similarly, one for whom the direction of prayer is ambiguous and he has no evidence at all: he acts by testimony of his heart without mere choice; because we said the correct direction is one of them, so the obligation did not drop, rather acting by testimony of his heart became obligatory. And if he acts by that: it is not permissible to overturn it except by a proof above it that necessitates overturning the first, so that it is not permissible to overturn a ruling passed by ijtihad by another like it; because the first was preponderated by acting by it, and conjecture is not overturned by certainty in the direction of prayer, because certainty is incidental and not contradictory, like a text revealed contrary to ijtihad, or consensus that is formed after the implementation of a ruling of ijtihad contrary to it. As for acting by it in the future contrary to the first: two types: if the ruling sought admits transition: acting by it is obligatory; otherwise: no. Explanation: the one who conjectures about the direction of prayer, if his conjecture changes: he acts by it in the future; because the ruling of direction admits transition from one direction to another, such that it transferred from the Sacred House to the Kaaba, and transferred from the exact location of the Kaaba to its direction, so conjecture becomes a proof contrary to the first. Similarly in all matters of ijtihad in legislated matters subject to transition and succession. As for what does not admit it: a man prayed in a garment based on conjecture about its purity in reality.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul deals with the nature of conflict (ta'arud) between different types of evidence. The author explains that when conflict arises between textual evidences from the Quran and Sunnah—such as two verses, two readings within a verse, two hadiths, or a hadith and a verse—the underlying cause is our ignorance of which one abrogates the other. This presumes that abrogation (naskh) is possible between such texts. However, when conflict arises between two analogical deductions (qiyasayn) or between two statements of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi), the resolution is different. Analogies cannot abrogate one another because qiyas itself is not a source of abrogation; it only extracts rulings. A Companion's statement is based on personal reasoning, so it is analogous to qiyas. When two analogies conflict, the mujtahid does not discard both; rather, he chooses whichever he finds more convincing by the 'testimony of his heart' (shahadat al-qalb). This is because in textual conflict, our ignorance is absolute and cannot serve as a proof, so we must seek the abrogating text. But in analogical conflict, the Law itself has permitted action based on ijtihad, recognizing that the truth is one but the mujtahid may hit or miss it, yet he is rewarded. Therefore, he is allowed to choose due to the semblance of truth (shubhat al-haqqiyyah) in his action. The 'testimony of the heart' is a valid proof in cases of necessity because the heart is endowed with intuitive insight (firasa). The author then gives examples: a traveler with two containers—one with impure water, one pure—and he doesn't know which is which. He cannot use either container, so he performs tayammum (ritual dry ablution) because he is unable to determine purity. Tayammum is a pure purifier in cases of inability. Here, conflict leads to inability (ajz), not necessity (darura), so qiyas (choosing by heart) is not allowed. But if he has two garments, one impure and one pure, and no other garments, he must perform taharri (conjecture) and choose one to wear, because he must cover himself out of necessity. Similarly, if the qibla direction is ambiguous with no external evidence, one must pray using his best judgment (taharri). Once a ruling is made by ijtihad, it cannot be overturned by another ijtihad of equal strength, because the first has been acted upon and thus becomes preponderant. However, if a stronger evidence (like a definitive text or consensus) comes later, it can overturn the first. For future actions, if the ruling admits of change (e.g., qibla direction can change as new evidence arises), then the new ijtihad is followed. If not (e.g., purity of a garment was determined by ijtihad and later certainty arises), the old ruling stands for the past but the new ruling applies for the future.

Key Terms
تعارض (ta'arud): Conflict or contradiction between two pieces of evidence that cannot be reconciled.
شهادة القلب (shahadat al-qalb): The intuitive conviction or testimony of the heart that inclines the mujtahid to prefer one evidence over another.
تحري (taharri): Conjecture or effort to determine the correct ruling or direction when evidence is ambiguous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding a mujtahid who faces conflict between two analogical deductions (qiyasayn)?
A) He must discard both and seek a new text.
B) He must follow the stronger analogy based on external criteria.
C) He may choose whichever he prefers by testimony of his heart.
D) He must follow the opinion of the majority of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The key distinction: textual conflicts are resolved by seeking abrogation because ignorance is absolute; conflicts of analogies are resolved by the heart's testimony because ijtihad is the basis and necessity permits it.

The Five Methods to Resolve Contradiction Between Evidences
Explaining the five ways to eliminate contradiction between conflicting proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five methods (al-makhlas) for resolving apparent contradiction (mu'arada) between two equal proofs, and apply the first two methods—by evidence strength and by ruling context—to given textual conflicts.

Core Idea
Apparent contradiction between equal proofs is resolved by one of five methods, not by discarding either proof—starting with checking if they are truly equal.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul outlines the foundational Hanafi approach to mu'arada (apparent contradiction). Instead of immediately invoking naskh or tarjih, the Hanafi school first checks whether a genuine contradiction exists by examining the evidence itself, the ruling, the context, time explicitly, or time implicitly. You will learn the logical sequence for diagnosing and resolving textual conflicts, with a focus on the first two methods which are elaborated here.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the structure of mu'arada
Understand that mu'arada requires two proofs of equal strength (i'tidal). If they are not balanced, no genuine contradiction exists, and the weaker is subordinated.
2
Identify the five methods
List the five perspectives: from the evidence (hujja), from the ruling (hukm), from the circumstance (hal), from time explicitly (zaman sarih), and from time implicitly (zaman dalala).
3
Apply the first method (min qibal al-hujja)
Compare the strength of the two proofs. If one is weaker (e.g., mujmal vs muhkam, or khabar wahid vs Quran/mutawatir), no contradiction exists; the stronger prevails or the weaker is interpreted harmoniously.
This method prevents hasty claims of contradiction.
4
Apply the second method (min qibal al-hukm)
If the rulings derived from the two proofs apply to different contexts (e.g., dar al-jaza' vs dar al-ibtila'), the contradiction disappears. Both are valid without conflict.
Example: the two oaths verses reconciled by abode of recompense vs trial.
5
Recognize the unelaborated methods
The author mentions hal, zaman sarih, and zaman dalala but does not detail them here. These are developed elsewhere in usul (e.g., contextual interpretation, naskh, or specification by time).
You will encounter them in more advanced studies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كيفية المَخلَص عن المعارضة : ] وإذا عرفت ركن المعارضة وشرطها وجب أن تبني عليه كيفية المَخلَص عن المعارضة على سبيل العدم من الأصل، وذلك خمسة أوجه : من قبل الحجة، ومن قبل الحكم، ومن قبل الحال، ومن قبل الزمان صريحاً، ومن قبل الزمان دلالةً. فقال: أطعم أهلك من سمين حُمُرك، فإنما حرَّمتُها من أجل جوالي القرية». فلم يوجد شرط المعارضة. تنزلنا، أليس فيه علة التحريم وهو كونها جلالة؟ ثم يقال: ما الموجب لترجيح التحريم في الأكل، وعدمه في السؤر؟ والله أعلم.

١- أما من قبل نفس الحجة فأن لا يعتدل الدليلان، فلا تقوم المعارضة، مثل المحكم يعارضه المجمل أو المتشابه. ومثل الكتاب أو المشهور من السنة يعارضهما خبر الواحد ؛ لأن ركنها اعتدال الدليلين، وأمثلة هذا كثيرةٌ لا تُحصى.

٢- وأما الحكم فإن الثابت بهما إذا اختلف عند التحقيق: سقط التعارض مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَكِن يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا كَسَبَتْ قُلُوبُكُمْ ﴾ البقرة / ٢٢٥ ، والمراد به الغموس. وقال جلَّ ذكره: لَا يُؤَاخِذُكُمُ اللهُ بِاللَّغْوِ فِي أَيْمَنِكُمْ وَلَكِن يُؤَاخِذُكُم بِمَا عَقَدتُّمُ الْأَيْمَنَ المائدة /۸۹ ، والغَموس داخل في هذا اللغو؛ لأن المؤاخذة المثبتة مطلقة، وهي في دار الجزاء، والمؤاخذة المنفية مقيدة بدار الابتلاء، فصح الجمع، وبطل التدافع، فلا يصح أن يُحمل البعض على البعض. وأمثاله كثيرة.
The method of escape from contradiction: And if you know the pillar of contradiction and its condition, you must build upon it the method of escape from contradiction in terms of non-existence from the origin, and that is five aspects: from the perspective of the evidence, from the perspective of the ruling, from the perspective of the circumstance, from the perspective of time explicitly, and from the perspective of time by implication. So he said: 'Feed your family from the fat of your donkey, for I have forbidden it because of the villagers' sheep.' So the condition of contradiction was not found. We assumed, does it not contain the cause of prohibition, i.e., it being a jallalah? Then it is said: What necessitates preferring prohibition in eating, but not in its saliva? And Allah knows best.

1. As for the perspective of the evidence itself: that the two proofs are not balanced, so contradiction does not occur, such as a muhkam (clear) text being opposed by a mujmal (ambiguous) or mutashabih (unclear) text. And like the Book or the well-known Sunnah being opposed by a khabar wahid (solitary report); because its pillar is the balance of the two proofs, and examples of this are numerous and incalculable.

2. As for the perspective of the ruling: that what is established by both, when they differ upon investigation, contradiction is dropped, such as His statement, the Exalted: {But He will take you to account for what your hearts have earned} [Al-Baqarah 2:225], and what is intended by it is the oath of falsehood (ghamus). And He, Exalted, said: {Allah will not take you to account for the vain in your oaths, but He will take you to account for what you have contracted the oaths} [Al-Ma'idah 5:89], and the false oath is included in this vain oath; because the affirmed accountability is absolute, and it is in the abode of recompense, and the negated accountability is restricted to the abode of trial. So the combination is correct, and the contradiction is invalidated, so it is not permissible to carry one part over the other. And examples of this are many.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage from al-Bazdawi's usul work presents the Hanafi method for resolving apparent contradictions between legal evidences (mu'arada). The author first states the general rule: once you understand the essential elements (rukn) and conditions (shart) of valid contradiction, you need to build upon that the method of resolution—specifically, how to eliminate the contradiction from its very origin. He then lists five approaches depending on the source of resolution: from the evidence itself, from the ruling, from the circumstance, from time explicitly, and from time by implication. An example is given involving a hadith about the donkey meat of a jallalah (an animal that feeds on impurities) where the condition for contradiction is absent. Then the first two methods are elaborated: (1) When the two evidences are not of equal strength, no real contradiction exists—e.g., a clear (muhkam) text versus an ambiguous (mujmal) text, or the Quran/mutawatir sunnah versus a solitary report (khabar wahid). (2) When the rulings derived from the two evidences are found to apply to different contexts—e.g., one verse (2:225) speaks of ultimate accountability for deliberate false oaths in the Hereafter, while another (5:89) speaks of legal liability for broken oaths in this world (expiation). The seeming contradiction disappears once we realize they address different spheres (dar al-jaza' vs. dar al-ibtila'), so both are valid without conflict.

Key Terms
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): Apparent contradiction between two equal evidences.
المخلَص (al-makhlas): The method or way out of a contradiction, specifically the five ways listed.
الحجة (al-hujja): The evidence or proof itself, considered from its strength and clarity.
الحكم (al-hukm): The legal ruling derived from the evidence, which may be applicable to different jurisdictions.
الحال (al-hal): The circumstance or situation that clarifies which meaning of a word applies (e.g., different readings of 'yathurna').
الزمان (al-zaman): Time; considered either explicitly (sarihan) or by implication (dalalatan) to resolve contradictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the first method to resolve a contradiction between two evidences?
A) By abrogation (naskh) of the weaker evidence.
B) By examining the evidence itself: if they are not of equal strength, no real contradiction exists.
C) By choosing the ruling that is easier for the people.
D) By consulting the consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
Apparent contradiction between equal proofs is resolved by five methods — first by checking evidence strength, then by examining ruling context, circumstance, or time — ensuring both proofs remain operative whenever possible.

Definition and Types of Bayan in Hanafi Usul
Defining bayan and its five types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define bayan in Hanafi usul, list its five types, and distinguish between bayan al-taqrir and bayan al-tafsir with examples.

Core Idea
Bayan is the act of clarifying a text, not its own clarity.

This lesson introduces a foundational concept in Hanafi usul: bayan (clarification). Understanding bayan is essential for knowing how ambiguous or general texts are made precise. Imam al-Bazdawi defines bayan and breaks it into five categories, explaining the first two in detail. You will learn the linguistic and technical meanings, the five types, and how the first two operate with Quranic and practical examples.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic and technical meanings
Identify that bayan literally means 'clarification' (izhar), not 'becoming manifest' (zuhur). In Hanafi usul, it refers to the act of clarifying a text, removing ambiguity or generalization.
The hadith 'In eloquence there is magic' supports the active sense.
2
Remember the five types of bayan
Memorize the five names: taqrir (confirmation), tafsir (interpretation), taghyir (alteration), tabdil (substitution), and darurah (necessity). Focus on the first two in this lesson.
The remaining three will be covered later.
3
Analyze examples of bayan al-taqrir
Notice that bayan al-taqrir attaches a word that cuts off any possibility of figurative or restricted meaning, confirming the obvious sense. Study the Quranic examples (angels all together, bird with wings) and the spoken examples (divorce, emancipation).
This type can be connected or disconnected from the clarified text.
4
Analyze examples of bayan al-tafsir
Recognize that bayan al-tafsir clarifies a mujmal (ambiguous) or mushtarak (homonymous) term. The Quranic commands for prayer and zakah are mujmal, and the Sunnah provides the details.
This type is typically separate (disconnected) clarification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب البيان
البيان في كلام العرب: عبارة عن الإظهار.
وقد يُستعمل في الظهور، قال الله تعالى: ﴿عَلَمَهُ الْبَيَانَ﴾ [الرحمن/4] و﴿هَذَا بَيَانُ لِلنَّاسِ﴾ [آل عمران/138]، وقال تعالى: ﴿ثُمَّ إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا بَيَانَهُ﴾ [القيامة/19].
والمراد بهذا كله : الإظهار والفصل.
وقد يُستعمل هذا مجاوزاً، و غير مجاوز، والمراد به في هذا الباب عندنا : الإظهار، دون الظهور.
ومنه قول النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام: (إن من البيان لسحراً)
أي الإظهار.
والبيان على أوجه: بيان تقرير وبيان تفسیر وبیان تغییر، وبيان تبديل، وبيان ضرورة، فهي خمسة أقسام.
أما بيان التقرير : فتفسيره : أن كل حقيقة تحتمل المجاز، أو عام يحتمل الخصوص إذا أُلحق به ما يقطع الاحتمال: كان بيان تقرير .
وذلك مثل قول الله تعالى: ﴿فَسَجَدَ الْمَلَيْكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ﴾ [الحجر/30]؛ لأن اسم الجمع كان عاماً يحتمل الخصوص، فقرره بذكر الكل.
ومثله قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا طَرٍ يَطِيرُ بِجَنَاحَيْهِ﴾ [الأنعام/38].
وذلك مثل أن يقول الرجل لامرأته: أنت طالق، وقال عَنيتُ به الطلاق من النكاح.
وإذا قال لعبده : أنتَ حرّ، وقال عَنيتُ به العتق عن الرق والملك.
وهذا البيان يصح موصولاً، ومفصولاً، لما قلنا إنه مقرر.
أما بيانُ التفسير : فبيانُ المجمَل والمشترك، مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ وَاتُوا الزَّكَوٰةَ﴾ [البقرة/110]، وَ﴿السَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ﴾ [المائدة/38]، ونحو ذلك، ثم لَحِقَه البيانُ بالسُّنَّة.
Chapter of Bayan. Bayan in the speech of the Arabs is an expression for clarification. And it is sometimes used for manifestation. Allah Most High said: 'He taught him the explanation' [al-Rahman:4] and 'This is a clarification for the people' [Aal Imran:138], and He said: 'Then indeed upon Us is its explanation' [al-Qiyama:19]. The intended meaning of all this is clarification and distinction. And this is sometimes used transitively and sometimes intransitively, and the intended meaning in this chapter according to us is clarification, not manifestation. And from it is the saying of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him: 'Indeed, in eloquence there is magic' meaning clarification. And bayan has categories: bayan of confirmation, bayan of interpretation, bayan of alteration, bayan of substitution, and bayan of necessity - thus they are five divisions. As for bayan of confirmation: its interpretation is that every literal meaning that admits figurative interpretation, or a general term that admits specification, if what cuts off the probability is attached to it, it becomes bayan of confirmation. Examples are the words of Allah Most High: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' [al-Hijr:30] because the collective noun was general and admitted specification, so He confirmed it by mentioning 'all'. And similarly His words: 'And no bird that flies with its wings' [al-An'am:38]. And an example is if a man says to his wife: 'You are divorced' and he says 'I meant by it the divorce from marriage.' And if he says to his slave: 'You are free' and he says 'I meant by it emancipation from slavery and ownership.' This bayan is valid whether connected or disconnected, because we have said it is confirmatory. As for bayan of interpretation: it is the clarification of the ambiguous and the homonym, such as the words of Allah Most High: 'Establish prayer and give zakah' [al-Baqarah:110] and 'The thief, male and female' [al-Ma'idah:38], and the like; then the clarification by the Sunnah followed.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is from Imam al-Bazdawi's work on Hanafi usul, introducing the chapter on bayan. The author first gives the linguistic definition of bayan as 'al-izhar' (clarification), citing Quranic verses and a hadith. He distinguishes bayan from mere appearance (zuhur) and states that in usul it means the act of clarifying. He then lists five types of bayan. The first type, bayan al-taqrir (confirmatory clarification), occurs when a text that could be ambiguous (like a literal word allowing metaphorical interpretation, or a general term allowing specification) is followed by something that removes that possibility. Examples include the verse using 'all of them together' to confirm the generality of 'angels', and a man's statement 'you are divorced' clarified by his intention. This type can be either connected or disconnected. The second type, bayan al-tafsir (interpretive clarification), clarifies a mujmal (ambiguous) or mushtarak (homonymous) term, like 'prayer' and 'zakah' which were explained by the Sunnah. The remaining three types (taghyir, tabdil, darurah) are not elaborated here but are defined in later sections. This passage is foundational for understanding how Hanafi scholars approach the clarification of legal texts.

Key Terms
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification, making something clear; here defined as 'al-izhar' (manifestation) but distinguished from 'al-zuhur' (becoming manifest).
بيان التقرير (bayan al-taqrir): Confirmatory clarification: attaching something that removes probability from a literal meaning or general term, confirming the intended meaning.
بيان التفسير (bayan al-tafsir): Interpretive clarification: clarifying a mujmal (ambiguous) or mushtarak (homonymous) term, often by the Sunnah.
مجمل (mujmal): A term that is ambiguous and requires clarification (bayan).
مشترك (mushtarak): A homonym, a word with multiple possible meanings, requiring clarification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes bayan al-taqrir from bayan al-tafsir?
A) Bayan al-taqrir is done by the Sunnah, while bayan al-tafsir is done by the Quran itself.
B) Bayan al-taqrir removes probability from a literal/general word, while bayan al-tafsir clarifies an ambiguous (mujmal) or homonymous (mushtarak) term.
C) Bayan al-taqrir only applies to the Prophet's sayings, while bayan al-tafsir applies to any text.
D) Bayan al-taqrir is a form of abrogation (naskh), while bayan al-tafsir is not.

Key Takeaway
Bayan is the act of clarifying a text; it has five types, with the first two (taqrir and tafsir) being the most fundamental in Hanafi usul.

Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir Defined
Defines and exemplifies two types of bayan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir, identify them in Qur'anic and fiqh examples, and apply the Hanafi rule that both are valid whether connected or disconnected.

Core Idea
Bayan al-Taqrir confirms the apparent meaning; Bayan al-Tafsir explains the ambiguous.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, bayan (clarification) is classified into five types. This lesson focuses on the first two: Bayan al-Taqrir (confirmatory clarification) and Bayan al-Tafsir (explanatory clarification). You will learn their definitions, conditions, and examples from the Qur'an and legal practice, and understand why both are considered valid even if the clarification is separated from the original statement.

Guided Path
1
Overview of the five types
Identify that the passage enumerates five types of bayan: taqrir, tafsir, taghyir, tabdil, and darura. Focus on the first two for this lesson.
The remaining three will be covered in subsequent lessons.
2
Define Bayan al-Taqrir
Understand that Bayan al-Taqrir applies when a statement that admits ambiguity (metaphor or specification of a general term) is reinforced by additional wording that removes all alternative interpretations. The clarification confirms the original intended meaning.
3
Analyze examples of Taqrir
Examine the Qur'anic verses: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' and 'no bird that flies with its two wings'. Also consider the fiqh example of a husband saying 'You are divorced' and clarifying 'from marriage'. Identify how each removes ambiguity.
The added words (e.g., 'all', 'with its two wings') cut off the possibility of metaphorical or specific interpretations.
4
Define Bayan al-Tafsir
Recognize that Bayan al-Tafsir explains a mujmal (ambiguous) or mushtarak (homonymous) term by providing its intended meaning. The clarification comes from an external source, often the Sunnah.
Examples include explaining the details of prayer and zakah, or clarifying a kinayah expression like 'bain' to mean divorce.
5
Note the Hanafi position on connected/disconnected bayan
Understand that both types of bayan are valid whether the clarification is connected to the original statement (mawsul) or delivered later (mafsul). This is a distinguishing feature of the Hanafi school.
The passage states 'this is a clear madhhab of our companions.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبيان على أوجه: بيان تقرير وبيان تفسیر وبیان تغییر، وبيان تبديل، وبيان ضرورة، فهي خمسة أقسام.
أما بيان التقرير: فتفسيره: أن كل حقيقة تحتمل المجاز، أو عام يحتمل الخصوص إذا أُلحق به ما يقطع الاحتمال: كان بيان تقرير. وذلك مثل قول الله تعالى: ﴿ فَسَجَدَ الْمَلَيْكَةُ كُلُّهُمْ أَجْمَعُونَ ﴾ الحجر / ٣٠؛ لأن اسم الجمع كان عاماً يحتمل الخصوص، فقرره بذكر الكل. ومثله قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا طَرٍ يَطِيرُ بِجَنَاحَيْهِ ﴾ الأنعام /٣٨. وذلك مثل أن يقول الرجل لامرأته: أنت طالق، وقال عَنيتُ به الطلاق من النكاح. وإذا قال لعبده : أنتَ حرّ، وقال عَنيتُ به العتق عن الرق والملك. وهذا البيان يصح موصولاً، ومفصولاً، لما قلنا إنه مقرر.
أما بيان التفسير: فبيان المجمَل والمشترك، مثل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَقِيمُوا الصَّلوةَ وَاتُوا الزَّكَوٰةَ﴾ البقرة / ١١٠، ﴿وَالسَّارِقُ وَالسَّارِقَةُ﴾ المائدة / ۳۸، ونحو ذلك، ثم لَحقَه البيان بالسُّنَّة. وذلك مثل قول الرجل لامرأته: أنت بائن إذا قال عَنيتُ به الطلاق: وكذلك في سائر الكنايات. ولفلان عليَّ ألف درهم وفي البلد نقود مختلفة، فإن بيانه بيان تفسير. ويصح هذا موصولاً ومفصولاً، هذا مذهب واضح لأصحابنا.
وأخرج الدارقطني عن عمرو بن شعيب عن أبيه عن جده: «أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أمَرَ بقطع السارق من الزَّنْد». وقد ذكرنا في تخريج أحاديث الاختيار ما في كل باب من الأبواب من الأحاديث، والله الموفق.
And the clarification (bayan) has aspects: Bayan al-Taqrir, Bayan al-Tafsir, Bayan al-Taghyir, Bayan al-Tabdil, and Bayan al-Darura; these are five divisions. As for Bayan al-Taqrir: its interpretation is that every reality that admits metaphor, or a general term that admits specification, if there is attached to it what cuts off the probability, it is Bayan al-Taqrir. That is like Allah's saying: 'So the angels prostrated, all of them together' (al-Hijr 30); because the collective noun was general admitting specification, so He reinforced it by mentioning 'all'. And similar is His saying: 'And no bird that flies with its two wings' (al-An'am 38). That is like a man saying to his wife: 'You are divorced,' and he says 'I meant thereby divorce from marriage.' And if he says to his slave: 'You are free,' and he says 'I meant thereby emancipation from bondage and ownership.' And this bayan is valid whether connected or disconnected, because we said it is confirmatory. As for Bayan al-Tafsir: it is the clarification of the mujmal and mushtarak, like Allah's saying: 'Establish prayer and give zakah' (al-Baqarah 110), 'The thief, male and female' (al-Ma'idah 38), and similar, then the clarification came by the Sunnah. That is like a man saying to his wife: 'You are bain,' if he says 'I meant thereby divorce'; and likewise for all kinayah expressions. And if someone says: 'So-and-so owes me one thousand dirhams,' while in the country there are different currencies, then its clarification is Bayan al-Tafsir. This is valid whether connected or disconnected; this is a clear madhhab of our companions. And al-Daraqutni narrated from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet ﷺ ordered cutting off the thief from the wrist. And we have mentioned in the takhrij of the ahadith of al-Ikhtiyar what is in each chapter of the chapters of the ahadith. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage from Imam al-Bazdawi's Usul defines the five types of bayan (clarification) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, but only elaborates on the first two: Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir. The passage type is an usul rule classification. The author lists the five types: Bayan al-Taqrir (confirmatory clarification), Bayan al-Tafsir (explanatory clarification), Bayan al-Taghyir (alteration), Bayan al-Tabdil (substitution), and Bayan al-Darura (necessity). He then explains Bayan al-Taqrir: it occurs when a statement that admits ambiguity (either metaphorical interpretation or specification of a general term) is reinforced by additional wording that removes all possibility of other meanings. The examples from the Qur'an show that Allah added 'all of them together' to the general noun 'angels' to confirm that every single angel prostrated. Similarly, the phrase 'with its two wings' confirms that the bird is a flying creature. In fiqh, if a man says 'You are divorced' and clarifies that he meant divorce from marriage, this is Bayan al-Taqrir because the word 'divorce' could refer to divorce from marriage or freeing from a commitment; the clarification confirms the intended meaning. This type of bayan is valid whether the clarification is connected to the statement or stated later (disconnected), because it merely confirms what was already intended. Next, Bayan al-Tafsir is used for mujmal (ambiguous) terms like 'prayer' and 'zakah' which need explanation of their details, and mushtarak (homonyms) like 'bain' which can mean different types of divorce. The Sunnah provides the explanatory details for these general commands. In the example of 'bain', the husband's statement is a kinayah that needs clarification; his specifying 'divorce' makes it a Bayan al-Tafsir. Similarly, for a debt of unspecified currency, clarification of the type of dirhams is Bayan al-Tafsir. This type is also valid whether connected or disconnected according to the Hanafi school. The passage then lists several hadith as evidence that the Sunnah provides Bayan al-Tafsir for Qur'anic injunctions, though the discussion is abbreviated. The teacher should note that the remaining three types (Taghyir, Tabdil, Darura) are not covered here but will be explained in subsequent lessons.

Key Terms
بيان التقرير (bayan al-taqrir): A clarification that removes possibility of metaphorical or specific interpretation by reinforcing the original statement.
بيان التفسير (bayan al-tafsir): A clarification that explains a mujmal (ambiguous) or mushtarak (homonymous) term by providing its intended meaning.
مجمَل (mujmal): A term that is ambiguous and requires external explanation to be understood.
مشترك (mushtarak): A homonymous term that has multiple distinct meanings, such as 'ayn (eye, spring, gold coin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following scenarios is an example of Bayan al-Tafsir?
A) The Qur'anic verse 'And no bird that flies with its two wings' (al-An'am 38).
B) A man says to his wife 'You are divorced' and later clarifies 'I meant divorce from marriage.'
C) The Prophet ﷺ explaining the number of rak'ahs in prayer after the command 'Establish prayer.'
D) A man says to his slave 'You are free' and later clarifies 'I meant emancipation.'

Key Takeaway
Bayan al-Taqrir and Bayan al-Tafsir are distinct types of clarification in Hanafi usul, both valid whether connected or disconnected, and essential for understanding how legal meanings are established from primary sources.

Takhsīs al-ʿĀmm: The Hanafi–Shafiʿī Dispute on Deferred Specification
Discusses the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether specification of a general can be deferred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafiʿī positions on deferred specification (tarākhī), apply the Hanafi ruling to a bequest scenario, and explain the epistemic basis for each position.

Core Idea
Specification of a general must be immediate; a deferred specification contradicts its definitive nature.

This passage dives into a core disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafiʿī schools: can a general command be specified by a later, separate statement? The answer reveals deep differences about the epistemic weight of the general. By working through the example of a bequest, we see the practical consequence of each school's position.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two positions: Hanafis say specification must be immediate (muttasil); Shafiʿīs allow both immediate and deferred (mutarākhī).
2
Examine the Hanafi proof
Analyze the bequest example: if connected, the second part specifies; if separated, it becomes a conflicting bequest. This shows that deferred specification is not recognized—it is treated as a new, independent ruling.
The will example illustrates the practical legal effect.
3
Examine the Shafiʿī proof
The Shafiʿī school points to the Quranic use of 'thumma' (then) in 'Then upon Us is its clarification' to argue that clarification (and thus specification) can be deferred.
The Hanafis respond that this applies only to pure bayan (clarification of ambiguous texts), not to specification of a general.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that if specification could be deferred, the general would not obligate a definitive ruling in the interim. But the general is like the specific in obligating definitively, so it cannot lose its force by a later statement.
Key: 'al-ʿāmm ʿindanā mithl al-khāṣṣ fī ījāb al-ḥukm qaṭʿan'
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: For Hanafis, a later statement cannot specify a general; it either abrogates (if later and contradictory) or stands as an independent command. For Shafiʿīs, the later statement can specify the general from the outset.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رحمهم الله ، حتى جعلوا البيان في الكنايات كلّها مقبولاً وإن فَصَل. قال الله تعالى: ثُمَّ إِنَّ عَلَيْنَا بَيَانَهُ القيامة/١٩، و: ثم: للتراخي، وهذا لأن الخطاب بالمجمل صحيح؛ لعقد القلب على حقية المراد به على انتظار البيان ألا يُرى أن ابتلاء القلب بالمتشابه للعزم على حقية المراد به صحيح في الكتاب والسنة من غير انتظار البيان، فهذا أولى، وإذا صح الابتلاء به : حَسُن القول بالتراخي. واختلفوا في خصوص العموم : فقال أصحابنا رحمهم الله : لا يقع الخصوص متراخياً. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : يجوز متصلاً، ومتراخياً. وقد قال علماؤنا رحمهم الله فيمن أوصى بهذا الخاتم لفلان، وبقصه : لفلان غيره موصولاً : إن الثاني يكون خصوصاً للأول، فيكون الفص للثاني. وإذا فَصَلَ : لم يكن خصوصاً، بل صار معارضاً، فيكون الفص بينهما. وهذا فرح لما مرَّ أن العموم عندنا مثلُ الخصوص في إيجاب الحكم قطعاً، ولو احتمل الخصوص متراخياً : لَما أوجب الحكم قطعاً، مثلُ العام الذي لحقه الخصوص. وعندهما سواء، ولا يوجب واحد منهما الحكم قطعاً، بخلاف لله الخصوص على ما مر. وليس هذا باختلاف في حكم البيان بل ما كان بياناً محضاً: القول فيه بالتراخي ؛ لأن البيان المحض من شرطه محل موصوف ببالإجمال والاشتراك ولا يجب العمل مع الإجمال والاشتراك فيحسن.
May Allah have mercy on them, until they made bayan in all kinayat acceptable even if separated. Allah Almighty said: 'Then upon Us is its clarification' (al-Qiyama 19), and 'thumma' (then) indicates deferral. And this is because addressing with the mujmal (ambiguous) is valid; due to the heart's resolve upon the truth of what is intended in anticipation of bayan. Do you not see that the heart's being tested with the mutashabih (ambiguous) for resolve upon the truth of what is intended is valid in the Book and Sunnah without awaiting bayan? So this is more appropriate. And if being tested with it is valid, then the statement allowing deferral is good. And they differed regarding specification of the general: our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) said: specification does not occur deferred. And al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it is permissible connected and deferred. And our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said regarding one who wills: 'This ring to so-and-so, and its gemstone to another,' if connected: then the second is specification of the first, so the gemstone goes to the second. And if separated: it is not specification, but becomes opposed, so the gemstone is between them. And this is a difference [perhaps 'farq' meaning distinction] because, according to us, the general is like the specific in necessitating the ruling definitively. And if specification were possible deferred, it would not necessitate the ruling definitively, like the general that has been specified. And according to them [the two companions], both are equal, and neither necessitates the ruling definitively, unlike contingent? specification as previously mentioned. And this is not a difference in the ruling of bayan; rather, what is pure bayan: the ruling regarding it is deferral, because pure bayan has the condition that it concerns something described by generality and commonality, and action is not obligatory with generality and commonality. So it is good.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage addresses a key usul dispute: Can takhsīs al-'āmm (specification of a general text) be deferred (mutarākhī) or must it be immediate (muttasil)? The Hanafi position (as held by Imam Abu Hanifa and his school) is that specification cannot be deferred; the general remains general until specification arrives, and if it is deferred, the general no longer obligates definitive action in the interim. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i permits both immediate and deferred specification. The Hanafis support their view with an example from wills: if someone says 'this ring to Zayd and its gemstone to 'Amr' in one connected statement, the gemstone goes to 'Amr as a specification of the first bequest. However, if the statements are separated (e.g., first 'ring to Zayd', later 'gemstone to 'Amr'), it is not considered specification but rather a conflicting bequest, so the gemstone is shared between them. This shows that deferred specification is not effective; instead, it results in a new independent ruling. The reasoning: for Hanafis, a general ('āmm) obligates a definitive ruling (qat'i), just like a specific (khāss). If specification could be deferred, the general would not have definitive force during the delay, which contradicts its nature. The Shafi'i view treats general as zanni (speculative) in its indication, so deferral is possible. The passage concludes by noting that pure bayan (clarification of a mujmal) is different: it can be deferred because the original text is inherently ambiguous and does not obligate action until clarification.

Key Terms
خصوص (takhsīs): The specification or particularization of a general (ʿāmm) text, restricting its application to some of its individuals or categories.
عموم (ʿumūm): A word that encompasses all individuals or categories it can apply to, e.g., 'every' or 'all'.
تراخي (tarākhī): Deferral or postponement of a clarifying statement to a later time, not immediately connected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a testator says: 'My ring to Zayd' (pause) and later says 'Its gemstone to 'Amr'?
A) The gemstone goes to 'Amr as a valid specification.
B) The gemstone is shared between Zayd and 'Amr.
C) The second bequest is invalid.
D) The ring goes to 'Amr instead.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a general text is definitive (qatʿī) and cannot be specified by a later separate statement; deferred specification transforms into a conflicting ruling rather than a specification.

Dispute on Delayed Specification of General Texts
Presents Hanafi-Shafi'i ikhtilaf on permissibility of delayed takhsis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the core disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on the permissibility of delayed takhsis of 'amm and explain the Hanafi position with its proof.

Core Idea
Specification of a definitive general text must be immediate; delay would undermine certainty.

This passage presents a foundational disagreement in usul al-fiqh: Can a general text ('amm) be specified (takhsis) by a later, separate revelation or statement? The Hanafis require immediate specification, while Imam al-Shafi'i allows it to be delayed. The dispute hinges on whether takhsis is a 'change' (taghyir) from certainty to probability, or a mere 'confirmation' (taqrir). We will work through the arguments, the famous 'ring and stone' analogy, and the reinterpretation of key Quranic proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify what each school holds regarding delayed takhsis. Hanafi: only immediate (muttasil). Shafi'i: both immediate and delayed (munfasil).
The Arabic terms: متصلاً vs متراخياً.
2
Understand the epistemological difference
The Hanafis consider 'amm to be definitive (qat'i) in its obligation until specified. The Shafi'is consider 'amm to be probabilistic (zanni). This difference drives the ruling on delay.
This is the root of the dispute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: the ring will
Examine the example: if someone bequeaths a ring and its stone in a single connected statement, the second specifies the first. If the statements are separated, the second becomes a competing claim, not a specification.
This illustrates why delay changes the nature of takhsis.
4
Examine the Shafi'i Quranic evidence
The Shafi'is cite the delayed clarification of the cow of Bani Israel and the specification of 'ahl' in the story of Nuh. Understand the apparent proof.
The text presents these as key proofs for the Shafi'i position.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response to these proofs
The Hanafis reinterpret the cow case as taqyid al-mutlaq (restriction of absolute) which is naskh, not takhsis. For the Nuh story, they argue that the specification was already connected via 'illa man sabaqa 'alayhi al-qawl' and that 'ahl' never included the disbelieving son.
This step shows how the Hanafis defend their position by reclassifying the evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في خصوص العموم : فقال أصحابنا رحمهم الله : لا يقع متراخياً. وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : يجوز متصلاً، ومتراخياً.
وقد قال علماؤنا رحمهم الله فيمن أوصى بهذا الخاتم لفلان، وبقصه : لفلان غيره موصولاً : إن الثاني يكون خصوصاً للأول، فيكون الفص للثاني. وإذا فَصَلَ : لم يكن خصوصاً، بل صار معارضاً، فيكون الفص بينهما.
وهذا فرح لما مرَّ أن العموم عندنا مثلُ الخصوص في إيجاب الحكم قطعاً، ولو احتمل الخصوص متراخياً : لَما أوجب الحكم قطعاً، مثلُ العام الذي لحقه الخصوص. وعندهما سواء، ولا يوجب واحد منهما الحكم قطعاً، بخلاف الخصوص على ما مر.
وليس هذا باختلاف في حكم البيان بل ما كان بياناً محضاً: القول فيه بالتراخي ؛ لأن البيان المحض من شرطه محل موصوف بالإجمال والاشتراك ولا يجب العمل مع الإجمال والاشتراك فيحسن القول بتراخي البيان ؛ ليكون الابتلاء بالعقد مرة، وبالفعل مع ذلك أخرى، وهذا مجمع عليه. وما ليس ببيان خالص محض، لكنه تغيير أو تبديل : لم يحتمل القول بالتراخي، بالإجماع على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
وإنما الاختلاف أن خصوص دليل العموم بيان، أو تغيير؟ فعندنا هو تغيير من القطع إلى الاحتمال فيُقيّد بالوصل، مثل الشرط والاستثناء. وعنده ليس بتغيير ؛ لما قلنا، بل هو تقرير، فصح موصولاً، ومفصولاً، ألا يُرى أنه يبقى على أصله في الإيجاب.
وقد استدل في هذا الباب بنصوص احتجنا إلى بيان تأويلها.
منها : أن بيان بقرة بني إسرئيل وقع متراخياً. وهذا عندنا تقييد للمطلق، وزيادة على النص، فكان نسخاً، فصح متراخياً ؛ لما نبين في بابه إن شاء الله تعالى.
واحتج بقوله تعالى في قصة نوح عليه السلام : ﴿فَأَسْلُكْ فِيهَا مِن كُل زَوْجَيْنِ اثْنَيْنِ وَأَهْلَكَ﴾ المؤمنون/27 : أن الأهل عام لحقه خصوص متراخ بقوله: ﴿إِنَّهُ لَيْسَ مِنْ أَهْلِكَ﴾ هود/46.
والجواب: أن البيان كان متصلاً به بقوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا مَن سَبَقَ عَلَيْهِ الْقَوْلُ﴾ هود/40، وذلك هو ما سبق من وعد إهلاك الكفار، وكان ابنه منهم. ولأن الأهل لم يكن متناولاً للابن؛ لأن أهل الرسل: من اتبعهم وآمن بهم.
They differed regarding specification (takhsis) of the general: Our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said: It does not occur delayed. And al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: It is permissible both connected and delayed. Our scholars said concerning one who bequeathed this ring to someone and its stone to another connectedly: The second is a specification of the first, so the stone goes to the second. If he separated [the statements], it is not a specification, but becomes opposing, so the stone is between them. This is a branch of what has passed: that the general with us is like the specific in obligating a ruling definitively, and if specification were possible delayed, it would not obligate the ruling definitively, like the general that is overtaken by specification. And with him [al-Shafi'i] both are equal, and neither obligates a ruling definitively, contrary to the specific as has passed. This is not a disagreement concerning the ruling of clarification (bayan); rather, what is pure clarification: the position on it is delayed, because pure clarification requires a locus described as ambiguous and shared, and acting upon ambiguity and sharing is not obligatory, so the position of delayed clarification is good, so that there is tribulation of the heart once and with action another time, and this is agreed upon. And what is not pure clarification, but is a change or substitution: it does not admit the position of delay by consensus, as we will explain if Allah wills. The only disagreement is whether specification of the general text is clarification or change. According to us, it is a change from certainty to probability, so it is restricted to connection, like condition and exception. According to him, it is not a change, as we said, but rather a confirmation, so it is valid both connected and disconnected. Do you not see that it remains upon its original [mode] of obligation. And proofs have been cited in this chapter which we need to explain their interpretation. Among them: that the clarification of the cow of the Children of Israel occurred delayed. This according to us is a restriction of the absolute and an addition to the text, so it was abrogation (naskh), so it was valid delayed, as we will explain in its chapter if Allah wills. And he argued by His statement in the story of Nuh (peace be upon him): "So embark therein of every kind two spouses and your family" (al-Mu'minun 27): that 'family' is general and was overtaken by a delayed specification by His statement: "Indeed, he is not of your family" (Hud 46). The answer: That the clarification was connected to it by His statement: "Except those upon whom the word has preceded" (Hud 40), and that is what preceded of the promise to destroy the disbelievers, and his son was among them. And because 'family' did not encompass the son, for the family of the messengers are those who follow them and believe in them.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage addresses a core usul dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding whether the specification (takhsis) of a general text ('amm) can occur with temporal separation (tarakhi) or must be immediate (ittisal). The passage begins by stating the two positions: the Hanafis hold that specification cannot be delayed; al-Shafi'i allows both immediate and delayed specification. To illustrate the practical implication, the Hanafis give an example from wills: if someone bequeaths a ring to one person and its stone to another in a single connected statement, the second bequest specifies the first, so the stone goes to the second. But if the statements are separated (i.e., not in the same utterance), the second is not a specification but a competing claim, and the stone is divided between them. The underlying principle is that according to the Hanafis, a general text is definitive (qat'i) in its obligation, just like a specific text. If delayed specification were possible, the general would not be definitively binding because one would always anticipate a possible exception. For al-Shafi'i, both general and specific are probabilistic (zanni), so delaying specification does not undermine certainty. The text then distinguishes between pure clarification (bayan mahd), which is agreed to be permissible with delay because it clarifies an ambiguous or shared term that does not require immediate action, and change or substitution (taghyir/tabdil), which cannot be delayed by consensus. The core of the dispute is whether takhsis of a general text is clarification or change. The Hanafis consider it a change because it transforms the ruling from certainty to probability, so it must be immediate like conditions and exceptions. Al-Shafi'i considers it a confirmation (taqrir) that leaves the original obligation intact, so delay is acceptable. Finally, the text addresses two Quranic proofs cited by the Shafi'is: the delayed clarification of the cow in Surah al-Baqarah, and the story of Nuh where 'family' (ahl) is general but later specified by 'he is not of your family'. The Hanafi response is that the cow case is not takhsis of a general but a restriction of an absolute (taqyid al-mutlaq) which is actually abrogation (naskh) and therefore permissible with delay. For the Nuh story, the specification was actually immediate because the exception 'except those upon whom the word has preceded' was already connected, and the son was among the disbelievers destined for destruction; moreover, the word 'ahl' (family) never included the son because the family of prophets are those who follow and believe.

Key Terms
العموم (al-‘umūm): A word that encompasses all its individuals without limitation; general text.
الخصوص (al-khuṣūṣ): Specification or specific text; also the act of specifying a general.
البيان المحض (al-bayān al-maḥḍ): Pure clarification that removes ambiguity from an ambiguous (mujmal) or shared (mushtarak) term.
التغيير (al-taghyīr): Change or alteration of a ruling from certainty to probability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must specification (takhsis) of a general text occur immediately rather than with delay?
A) Because the general text is ambiguous (mujmal) and requires immediate clarification.
B) Because the general text is definitive (qat'i) in its ruling, and delayed specification would undermine that certainty.
C) Because the Shafi'i school agrees that delay is not allowed.
D) Because the Quranic examples all show immediate specification.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires takhsis of a general text to be immediate because 'amm is definitive (qat'i) and delayed takhsis would turn certainty into probability, contradicting the nature of change (taghyir) which must be connected.

Is Takhsis of 'Amm Bayan or Taghyir? The Hanafi View
Debating whether takhsis of 'amm is bayan or taghyir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle that takhsis of a general text ('amm) is a change (taghyir) from certainty to probability, requiring immediate connection, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Specification of a general text changes certainty to probability — it is taghyir, not bayan, so it cannot be delayed.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul addresses a central dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: When a general text ('amm) is followed by a specification (takhsis), does that specification merely clarify the intended meaning (bayan) or does it change the original ruling category? The answer determines whether the specification can be delayed (tarakhi) or must be immediately connected (muwasala). The Hanafi school insists on immediate connection because a general text gives certainty (qat'), and specification introduces probability (zann), thus it is a change, not mere clarification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core disagreement
Recognize that the dispute is whether takhsis of 'amm is bayan (clarification) or taghyir (change). Hanafi holds taghyir; Shafi'i holds bayan.
The term 'bayān' here means pure clarification that does not alter the ruling's certainty.
2
State the Hanafi position and rationale
For Hanafis, 'amm gives qat' certainty; takhsis introduces zann, thus it changes the ruling from qat' to zann. Hence it is a taghyir that must be connected like a condition or exception.
This is based on the consensus that pure clarification can be delayed, but change cannot.
3
Examine the Shafi'i Quranic proofs
Analyze the four examples cited by opponents: the cow of Bani Israel, Noah's family, the verse about worshippers, and the village of Lot. Each appears to be a delayed specification.
These examples are meant to show that specification can be detached from the general text.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
For each example, see how the Hanafi refutes: either it involves restriction of mutlaq (naskh), the specification was connected implicitly, or the general term never included the specified items.
For instance, 'family' in Noah's story means followers of religion, not blood relatives.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If a general text is revealed and a specification comes later, Hanafis hold the general applies until the specification arrives; Shafi'is can apply the specification retroactively.
This affects how we understand the chronology of revelation and legal derivation.
