And the claim of delay of clarification, so that the trial be with the contract once, and with the action along with that another time, and this is agreed upon. And what is not pure and clear clarification, but rather a change or substitution: it does not allow the claim of delay, by consensus, as we will explain if Allah wills. And the disagreement is only whether specification of a general text is clarification or change? According to us, it is a change from certainty to probability, so it is restricted to connection, like the condition and exception. According to him (the opponent), it is not a change, as we said, but rather it is a confirmation, so it is valid whether connected or separated. Do you not see that it remains upon its original in obligation? And proofs have been adduced in this chapter that we need to explain their interpretation. Among them: that the clarification of the cow of the Children of Israel occurred with delay. And according to us, this is a restriction of the absolute and an addition to the text, so it was abrogation, so it is valid with delay, as we will explain in its chapter if Allah wills. And he argued with His statement, exalted, in the story of Noah, peace be upon him: 'So embark therein of each kind two, two, and your family' (Quran 23:27): that 'family' is general and was specified with delay by His statement: 'Indeed, he is not of your family' (Quran 11:46). The answer: the clarification was connected to it by His statement, exalted: 'Except those upon whom the word has preceded' (Quran 11:40), and that is what preceded of the promise to destroy the disbelievers, and his son was among them. And because 'family' did not include the son; because the family of the messengers are those who follow them and believe in them, so it is a family of religion, not lineage. Except that Noah said in what is narrated from him: 'Indeed, my son is of my family' (Quran 11:45), because he had called him to faith, so when Allah revealed the great verse (the flood), his assumption about him improved and his hope extended towards him, so he built his request upon that. When his matter became clear to him, he turned away from him and surrendered him to punishment. And this is permissible in the dealings of the messengers, peace be upon them, based on human knowledge until revelation descends, as Allah said: 'And the forgiveness of Abraham for his father was not except due to a promise he had made to him. But when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of Allah, he disassociated from him' (Quran 9:114). And he argued with His statement: 'Indeed, you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell' (Quran 21:98), then specification followed it with delay by His statement: 'Indeed, those for whom the best from Us has preceded' (Quran 21:101). This argument is invalid according to us; because the beginning of the verse did not include Jesus and the angels, peace be upon them; because the word 'ma' is for non-rational beings, but they (the opponents) were obstinate, so He increased in clarification to turn away from their obstinacy. And he argued with His statement: 'Indeed, we will destroy the people of this village' (Quran 29:31), and this is general from which the family of Lot, peace be upon him, was specified with delay. This is also incorrect; because the clarification was connected to it; as for this verse: because He said: 'Indeed, its people are wrongdoers' (Quran 29:31), and that is an explicit exception.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the nature of specification (takhsis) of a general text ('amm). The author begins by stating a consensus: any clarification that is truly a clarification (bayan) can be delayed, as it tests the listener with both the general contract and the specific action separately. However, if the so-called 'clarification' is actually a change (taghyir) or substitution, then it cannot be delayed by consensus. The core disagreement is whether specifying a general text falls under clarification or change. The Hanafi position (indicated by 'indana) holds that takhsis is a change from certainty (qat') to probability (zann) because the general text gives certainty in its generality, and specification introduces probability; thus it must be immediately connected (muwasala) to the original text, like a condition or exception. The opponent (likely the Shafi'i school) argues that specification is not a change but a confirmation (taqrir) that leaves the original ruling intact, so it can be delayed.

The author then refutes several proofs adduced by opponents. First, the story of the cow of Bani Israel: a delayed specification of an absolute command. The Hanafi response is that this is not a case of takhsis of 'amm but rather restriction of a mutlaq, which is considered an addition to the text and thus abrogation (naskh), which can indeed be delayed. Second, the verse of Noah: 'So embark therein... your family' was general and later specified that his son was not included. The Hanafi response provides a double rebuttal: (a) the specification was actually connected through the exception 'except those upon whom the word has preceded', and Noah's son was among them, so the exception was present from the start; (b) the word 'ahl' (family) in the Quran for prophets means followers in faith (ahl al-din), not blood relatives. Noah's statement 'my son is of my family' was based on his human hope, but clarified by revelation. Third, the verse 'You and what you worship... are fuel of Hell' followed by the exception 'those for whom the best has preceded' seems delayed. The Hanafi response argues that the word 'ma' (what) in Arabic is for non-rational beings, so the verse never included Jesus and the angels (who are rational). Hence the later verse was just extra explanation, not a specification. Fourth, the verse about destroying the people of the village with an exception for Lot's family. The Hanafi says the exception was actually connected because the verse itself states 'its people are wrongdoers', which implicitly excludes the righteous Lot. Thus in all cases, the specification was either not a true change, or it was connected. This reinforces the Hanafi usul that takhsis of 'amm must be immediate to preserve the certainty of the general.

Key Terms
بيان (bayān): Clarification that brings out the intended meaning of a text without altering its ruling category.
تخصيص (takhṣīṣ): Specification that excludes some members of a general category from the ruling.
تراخي (tarākhin): Delay of clarification from the original text.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation, which for Hanafis includes addition to the text (ziyada 'ala al-nass) and thus can be delayed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why does the specification (takhsis) of a general text ('amm) require immediate connection (muwasala)?
A) Because it is a pure clarification (bayan) that can be delayed.
B) Because it is a change (taghyir) from certainty (qat') to probability (zann).
C) Because it is considered abrogation (naskh).
D) Because the Quranic examples demand it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that specification ('takhsis') of a general text ('amm') is a change (taghyir) in the ruling's certainty level, not a mere clarification (bayan), and therefore must be immediately connected to the original text.

Hanafi Rejection of Delayed Specification: The Case of Al-Anbiya 98
Opponent's proof using delayed specification and Hanafi refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the dispute over delayed specification (takhsis mutarrakhi) by identifying the Hanafi linguistic argument using 'ma' and distinguishing it from the Shafi'i position based on the verse Al-Anbiya 98-101.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school rejects delayed specification because the word 'ma' inherently excludes intelligent beings, so the general never applied to them — no delay occurred.

In this passage, we examine a classical usul dispute: Can a general text be specified by a later revelation? The Shafi'i school argues yes, citing the verse 'Indeed you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell' (98), which they claim was later specified to exclude Jesus and the angels by verse 101. The Hanafi school refutes this by focusing on the Arabic word 'ma' (what), which is used exclusively for non-intelligent beings. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and logical underpinnings of the Hanafi argument.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on delayed specification
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that specification must be connected (mutassil) to the general statement; delayed specification (takhsis mutarrakhi) is invalid.
This is a foundational usul rule differentiating Hanafi from Shafi'i methodology.
2
Identify the opponent's argument and evidence
The opponent (Shafi'i) uses the verse Al-Anbiya 98 as a general statement, then points to verse 101 as a later specification. They also invoke the stories of Noah and Abraham as examples of delayed clarification.
The opponent's dalil is both textual (the verses) and analogical (prophetic precedent).
3
Analyse the Hanafi response: the linguistic argument
The Hanafi response centres on the word 'ma' (ما) in verse 98. In Arabic, 'ma' is used for non-intelligent beings. Since Jesus and angels are intelligent, the verse never included them. Thus, verse 101 is not a delayed specification but an additional clarification (bayan) addressing obstinacy.
This is a key point: the general statement was never truly general over all beings due to the linguistic scope of 'ma'.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response: the prophetic stories
The Hanafi response argues that the stories of Noah and Abraham are based on human knowledge (ilm bashari) and not legal rulings. Prophets acted on their limited knowledge until revelation clarified the truth. These examples do not establish a precedent for delayed specification in legal texts.
This distinguishes between factual judgment (based on human knowledge) and legal ruling (based on divine specification).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If delayed specification were valid, a general legal text could be applied until the specification arrives, potentially leading to incorrect rulings in the interim. The Hanafi position ensures that if the text is truly general, its scope is fixed from the outset.
This highlights the practical impact: the difference affects how jurists interpret general commands before any later specification is revealed.

Source Text

إلا أن نوحاً عليه السلام قال فيما حكى عنه : {وَإِنَّ ابْنِي مِنْ أَهْلِي} [هود: 45]، لأنه كان دعاه إلى الإيمان، فلما أنزل الله تعالى الآية الكبرى: حسن ظنه به، وامتد نحوه رجاؤه، فبنى عليه سؤاله، فلما وضح له أمره: الله أعرض عنه، عنه، وسلمه للعذاب، وهذا سائغ في معاملات الرسل عليهم السلام؛ بناء على العلم البشري إلى أن ينزل الوحي، كما قال الله تعالى: {وَمَا كَانَ اسْتِغْفَارُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ لِأَبِيهِ إِلَّا عَن مَّوْعِدَةٍ وَعَدَهَا إِيَّاهُ فَلَمَّا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ أَنَّهُ عَدُوٌّ لِّلَّهِ تَبَرَّأَ مِنْهُ} [التوبة: 114]. واحتج بقوله تعالى: {إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ حَصَبُ جَهَنَّمَ} [الأنبياء: 98]، ثم لحقه الخصوص بقوله تعالى: {إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُم مِّنَّا الْحُسْنَى} [الأنبياء: 101]، متراخياً عن الأول. وهذا الاستدلال باطل عندنا؛ لأن صدر الآية لم يكن متناولاً لعيسى والملائكة عليهم السلام؛ لأن كلمة ما لذوات غير العقلاء، لكنهم كانوا متعنتين، فزاد في البيان؛ إعراضاً عن تعنتهم.
Except that Noah, peace be upon him, said in what is narrated about him: 'Indeed my son is of my family' (Hud 45), because he had called him to faith. When Allah revealed the great verse, he had good opinion of him, and his hope extended towards him, so he built his request upon that. Commentary
This passage presents an opponent's argument (likely from the Shafi'i school) attempting to prove the validity of delayed specification (takhsis mutarrakhi) using the story of Noah and Abraham, and specifically the verse 'Indeed you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell' (Al-Anbiya 98). The opponent claims that this verse is general, then later specified by verse 101 'Indeed those for whom the best has preceded from Us' which excludes Jesus and the angels, and that this specification came after a delay. The Hanafi response refutes this by arguing that the word 'ma' (what) in Arabic is used for non-intelligent beings, so the verse never included intelligent beings like Jesus and angels. Therefore, there was no delayed specification; rather, the clause in verse 101 is an additional clarification (bayan) to counter the obstinacy of the opponents. The examples of Noah and Abraham are used to show that prophets may act on human knowledge until revelation clarifies the truth, but these are not precedents for delayed specification in legal rulings.

Key Terms
ما (ma): The word 'ma' in Arabic is used for non-intelligent beings (ghayr al-'uqala')
تخصيص متراخ (takhsis mutarrakhi): Specification of a general text that occurs after a delay from the original utterance
بيان (bayan): Clarification or explanation of a text, often used to describe the role of verse 101 as clarifying the scope of verse 98

Why does the Hanafi school reject the opponent's argument using the verse 'Indeed you and what you worship...'?
A) Because the verse was abrogated before specification
B) Because the word 'ma' excludes intelligent beings, so the general never included Jesus and angels
C) Because the specification came in the same verse without delay
D) Because the verse is not general at all

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rejection of delayed specification (takhsis mutarrakhi) is rooted in the linguistic precision of Quranic Arabic: the word 'ma' limits the generality to non-intelligent beings, making any later 'specification' a mere clarification of the original intended scope.

Hanafi Refutation of Delayed Specification in Verse on Destroying a Town
Opponent's second proof on delayed specification and Hanafi response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify an alleged case of delayed specification and apply the Hanafi rule that the bayan must be muttasil to reject it.

Core Idea
A general statement with an implicit immediate exception is not delayed specification.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: whether a general Quranic verse can be specified by a later, separate revelation. The opponent cites the story of Lut as proof that delayed specification is valid. The Hanafi school responds by showing that the specification was actually connected within the same verse, thereby preserving the principle that bayan must be muttasil. Understanding this argument strengthens your ability to analyze textual evidence in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent argues that the general command to destroy a town (Al-Ankabut 31) was later specified to exclude Lut's family, proving delayed specification is valid.
This is a classic argument against the Hanafi requirement of muttasil bayan.
2
Locate the general statement
The verse says: 'Indeed We are going to destroy the people of this town.' This is a general (amm) statement concerning all inhabitants.
3
Find the alleged delayed specification
The specification of Lut's family appears in other verses (e.g., Al-Hijr 59-60), which the opponent claims is a delayed bayan.
4
Apply the Hanafi principle of muttasil bayan
Hanafi usul requires that the bayan (specification) be connected (muttasil) to the general statement. The verse itself contains the phrase 'its people were wrongdoers,' which is an immediate exception — the destruction applies only to wrongdoers, excluding the righteous family of Lut from the outset.
Thus, the specification was never delayed; it was inherent in the same utterance.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
If delayed specification were allowed, general texts would remain uncertain until a later specification, undermining their immediate applicability. The Hanafi position ensures legal certainty by requiring the specification to be connected.
This practical consequence (thamarah) strengthens the Hanafi argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج بقوله تعالى: {إِنَّا مُهْلِكُوا أَهْلِ هَذِهِ الْقَرْيَةِ} [العنكبوت: 31]، وهذا عام خُص منه آل لوط عليه السلام متراخياً. وهذا أيضاً غير صحيح؛ لأن البيان كان متصلاً به، أما في هذه الآية: فلأنه قال: {إِنَّ أَهْلَهَا كَانُوا ظَالِمِينَ} [العنكبوت: 31]، وذلك استثناء واضح.
And he argued with His statement: 'Indeed We are going to destroy the people of this town' (Al-Ankabut 31), and this is general from which the family of Lot, peace be upon him, were specified delayed. And this also is not correct, because the clarification was connected to it. As for this verse: because He said: 'Indeed its people were wrongdoers' (Al-Ankabut 31), and that is a clear exception.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This lesson presents another opponent's proof for delayed specification. The opponent cites the verse where Allah tells Abraham that He will destroy the people of a certain town, which is a general statement. Then later, the family of Lut is excluded (as in other verses like Al-Hijr 59-60). The opponent claims this is a case of delayed specification. The Hanafi response argues that the clarification was actually connected (mutassil) to the general statement. In this very verse, Allah says 'indeed its people were wrongdoers,' which is an explicit exception—the verse itself specifies that the destruction is for wrongdoers, so the family of Lut (believers) were never included. Thus, the specification was not delayed but inherent in the same utterance.

Key Terms
البيان المتصل (al-bayan al-muttasil): A clarification that is connected to the general statement without delay, either in the same utterance or immediately adjacent.
استثناء متصل (istithna' muttasil): A connected exception that immediately qualifies a general statement within the same utterance.

B) Because the verse includes the phrase 'its people were wrongdoers,' which is a clear exception
C) Because the family of Lut were never mentioned in the verse
D) Because the verse was general and then specified by the Prophet's hadith

The Hanafi Classification of 'Qurba' as Mujmal Clarified by Hadith
A dispute over whether a hadith specifies a general verse or clarifies an ambiguous term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between takhsis of an 'amm and bayan of a mujmal by applying the Hanafi usul principle to the verse of khums.

Core Idea
A term with multiple possible meanings is mujmal, not 'amm; clarification is not specification.

In usul al-fiqh, the classification of a term as 'amm (general) or mujmal (ambiguous) determines how later texts interact with it. The opponent cites the khums verse and a hadith to argue for delayed specification; the Hanafi response reclassifies the term as mujmal, turning the hadith into clarification. This lesson will walk through the dispute and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's argument
Recognize that the opponent cites the verse 'wa li dhil qurba' as general and the hadith as specifying only some relatives, implying delayed specification is valid.
The opponent believes 'qurba' is 'amm.
2
Identify the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position is that 'qurba' is mujmal (ambiguous) because it can mean various types of closeness, so the hadith clarifies its intended meaning.
The hadith explains 'qurba' means 'qurba al-nusra' (kinship of support).
3
Understand the distinction between 'amm and mujmal
An 'amm term covers all its instances definitively; a mujmal term has no clear meaning until clarified. In Hanafi usul, mujmal requires bayan, not takhsis.
This distinction is critical to the tarjih.
4
Apply the distinction to the verse and hadith
Analyze the word 'qurba' – it can refer to blood relatives, support, or other connections. The hadith narrows it to those who supported the Prophet, thus clarifying the ambiguity.
The Prophet's distribution to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib illustrates the criterion.
5
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf
If the hadith is takhsis, delayed specification is allowed; if it is bayan, the ruling does not support delayed specification. The Hanafi view affirms that 'qurba' was always intended for supporters.
The practical effect is on how khums is allocated today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج بقوله تعالى: {وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى} [الأنفال: 41] أنه خُص منه بعض قرابة النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام بحديث ابن عباس في قصة عثمان وجبير بن مطعم رضي الله عنهم. وهذا عندنا من قبيل بيان المُجمَل؛ لأن القربى مجمل، وكان الحديث بياناً له أن المراد به: قربى النُّصرة، لا قربى القرابة، وإجماله: أن القربى يتناول غير النسب، ويتناول وجوهاً من النسب مختلفة، والله أعلم. (1) قصة عثمان وجبير: عن جبير بن مطعم قال: لما قسَمَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سهم ذوي القربى من خيبر بين بني هاشم وبني المطلب، جئتُ أنا وعثمان ابن عفان فقلنا: يا رسول الله! هؤلاء بنو هاشم لا ننكر فضلهم؛ لمكانك فما منهم، بال إخواننا من بني المطلب أعطيتهم، وتركتنا وإنما نحن وهم بمنزلة واحدة؟! فقال: 'إنهم لم يفارقوني في الجاهلية والإسلام، وإنما بنو هاشم وبنو المطلب شيء واحد، ثم شبك بين أصابعه'. رواه أبو داود والنسائي وابن ماجه وهو للبخاري باختصار سياق، وقال البرقاني: هو على شرط مسلم.
And he argued with His statement: 'And for the kinsfolk' (Al-Anfal 41) that some relatives of the Prophet, peace be upon him, were specified from it by the hadith of Ibn Abbas in the story of Uthman and Jubayr ibn Mut'im, may Allah be pleased with them. And this, according to us, is of the category of clarification of the ambiguous (mujmal), because 'qurba' is ambiguous, and the hadith was a clarification for it that what is meant is 'kinship of support,' not kinship of lineage. And its ambiguity is that 'qurba' includes non-lineage relationships and includes various aspects of lineage. And Allah knows best. (1) The story of Uthman and Jubayr: from Jubayr ibn Mut'im who said: When the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, distributed the share of the kinsfolk from Khaybar among Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, I and Uthman ibn Affan came and said: O Messenger of Allah! These Banu Hashim, we do not deny their virtue because of your position, but why did you give to our brothers from Banu al-Muttalib and leave us, while we and they are in the same position? He said: 'They did not leave me in the Jahiliyyah and Islam, and Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib are one thing,' then he interlaced his fingers. Narrated by Abu Dawud, al-Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah, and it is in al-Bukhari with a shortened context, and al-Barqani said: It is upon the condition of Muslim.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This is the third opponent's argument for delayed specification. The opponent cites the verse 'and for the kinsfolk' (Al-Anfal 41) regarding the khums (one-fifth) and claims that some relatives of the Prophet were excluded from this general term by the hadith of Ibn Abbas about Uthman and Jubayr, implying that the specification came later. The Hanafi response reclassifies this as a case of clarification (bayan) of an ambiguous term (mujmal), not specification of a general term. The word 'qurba' (kinsfolk) is ambiguous; it can mean both lineage and non-lineage relationships. The hadith clarifies that what is meant is 'qurba al-nusra' (kinship of support), i.e., those who supported the Prophet in hardship, not simply blood relatives. Thus, the hadith does not specify a general term but explains an ambiguous one. The footnote includes the full hadith where the Prophet gave to Banu Hashim and Banu al-Muttalib, excluding other Quraysh, indicating that support in the pre-Islamic and Islamic periods was the criterion.

Key Terms
مُجْمَل (mujmal): A term that is ambiguous and requires clarification from another source
قربى النصرة (qurba al-nusra): Kinship based on support and allegiance, not blood lineage
بيان (bayan): Clarification of an ambiguous term by an authoritative source
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term by restricting its application

C) Because the hadith was revealed before the verse
D) Because the verse was specifically about Banu Hashim only

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi distinction between mujmal and 'amm determines whether a later text is clarification or specification.

Exception as Clarification, Not Contradiction
Defending Hanafi view: exception is extraction and clarification, not contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that exception (istithna) is a clarification of the remainder, not a contradiction, and distinguish it from independent specification (takhsis).

Core Idea
Exception extracts and clarifies the remainder; it does not contradict or nullify the original general statement.

In Hanafi usul, the nature of exception is a critical point of disagreement with other schools. This passage defends the view that exception (istithna) is not a contradiction (mu'arada) but rather a linguistic device that extracts the excepted part and speaks about the remainder. The author presents textual, consensus, and rational proofs to show that exception is dependent on the preceding statement and does not function independently like a specification text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the nature of exception? Is it a contradiction that nullifies the ruling from the excepted part, or is it an extraction that clarifies the remainder?
The passage addresses the Hanafi view vs. an opposing view (likely Mutakallimin).
2
Follow the first argument: speech remains
Exception does not remove the speech itself from the beginning of the statement; the original wording persists. Only the ruling may be prevented, but the speech remains intact.
This contrasts with abrogation (naskh), which removes the ruling entirely.
3
Examine the textual proof
The Quranic verse (al-Ankabut 14) uses exception: 'a thousand years except fifty'. The exception does not negate the 'thousand' but limits it. In reports (akhbar), the ruling persists despite the exception.
The Hanafi view emphasizes that exception is a limit (ghaya), not a nullification.
4
Analyze the consensus proof
All linguists agree that exception is extraction (istikhraj) and speech about the remainder after exclusion. This supports the Hanafi interpretation that exception clarifies rather than contradicts.
The combination of extraction and speech about the remainder is obligatory.
5
Understand the three rational proofs
(1) Contradiction applies equally to part and whole (like naskh), but exception from the whole is invalid. (2) A contradictory proof is independent, but exception depends on the preceding statement. (3) Speech without ruling is possible (e.g., child's divorce), so the issue is preponderance, not impossibility.
These proofs collectively show that exception cannot be a contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك : لا عالم إلا زيد: أي فإنه عالم.
وأما الثالث: فلأنا نجد الاستثناء لا يرفع التكلم بقدره من صدر الكلام، وإذا بقي التكلم صيغة : بقي بحكمه، فلا سبيل إلى رفع التكلم، بل تجب المعارضة بحكمه فامتناع الحكم مع قيام التكلم سائغ، فأما انعدام التكلم مع وجوده: فمما لا يُعقل.
واحتج أصحابنا رحمهم الله بالنص والإجماع، والدليل المعقول.
أما النص: فقوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خَمْسِينَ عَامًا﴾ [العنكبوت: ١٤]، وسقوط الحكم بطريق المعارضة في الإيجاب يكون لا في الأخبار، فبقاء التكلم بحكمه في الخبر : لا يقبل الامتناع بمانع.
وأما الإجماع: فقد قال أهل اللغة قاطبةً : إن الاستثناء استخراج وتكلّم بالباقي بعد الثنيا، وإذا ثبت الوجهان وجب الجمع بينهما، فقلنا إنه استخراج، وتكلّم بالباقي بوضعه، وإثبات ونفي بإشارته، على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى.
وأما الدليل المعقول فوجوه :
أحدها: أن ما يمنع الحكم بطريق المعارضة: استوى فيه البعض والكل، كالنسخ ، ولم يستو هنا ؛ لأن الاستثناء من الكل باطل.
والثاني: أن دليل المعارضة ما يستقل بنفسه، مثل دليل الخصوص والاستثناء قط لا يستقل بنفسه، وإنما يتمُّ بما قبله، فلم يصلح معارضاً، لكنه لما كان لا يجوز الحكم ببعض الجملة حتى تتم، كما لا يجوز الحكم ببعض الكلمة حتى تنتهي : احتمل وقف أول الكلام على آخره حتى يتبين بآخره المراد بأوله، وهذا الإبطال طريقة مذهب الخصم.
والثالث: لتصحيح ما قلنا، وبيان ذلك وهو أن وجود التكلم ولا حكم : له أصلاً، ولا انعقادَ له بحكمه أصلاً سائغ، مثل الامتناع بالمعارض ،بالإجماع مثل طلاق الصبي ،وإعتاقه، وإنما الشأن في الترجيح.
وبيانه: أن الاستثناء متى جُعل معارضاً في الحكم بقي التكلم بحكمه في صدر الكلام، ثم لا يبقى من الحكم إلا بعضه، وذلك لا يصلح حكماً لكل التكلم بصدره. ألا يُرى أن الألف اسم علم له لا يقع على غيره، ولا يحتمله : لا يجوز أن تسمى التسعمائة ألفاً، بخلاف دليل الخصوص؛ لأنه إذا عارض العموم في بعض : بقي الحكم المطلوب وراء دليل الخصوص ثابتاً بذلك بعينه، صالحاً لأن يثبت به كاسم المشركين إذا خُص منه نوع: كان الاسم واقعاً على الباقي بلا خلل.
ولهذا قلنا إن العام إذا كان كلمة فرد، أو اسم جنس: صح إلى أن ينتهي بالفرد، وإذا كانت صيغة جمع: انتهى الخصوص إلى الثلاثة، لا غير، فلذلك بطل أن يكون معارضاً، فجعل تكلُّماً بالباقي بحقيقته وصيغته، وكان طريقاً في اللغة يطول مرةً، ويقصر أخرى، وجعل للإيجاب والنفي بإشارته.
وبيانه أن الاستثناء بمنزلة الغاية للمستثنى منه، ألا يُرى أن الأول به وهذا لأن الاستثناء يدخل على نفي أو إثبات والإثبات بالعدم ينتهي، والعدم بالوجود ينتهي، وإذا كان الوجود غايةً للأول، أو العدمُ ينتهي.
And likewise: 'There is no scholar except Zayd' means that he is a scholar. As for the third: because we find that exception does not remove the speech from its presumed scope in the beginning of the statement. When the speech remains as a form, it remains with its ruling. There is no way to remove the speech; rather, contradiction must be in its ruling. So the prevention of the ruling while the speech exists is permissible. But the non-existence of the speech while it exists is unintelligible. Our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) argued with text, consensus, and rational proof. As for the text: the saying of Allah: 'So he remained among them a thousand years except fifty years' [al-Ankabut:14]. And the omission of the ruling through contradiction in affirmatives is not in reports. So the survival of the speech with its ruling in a report does not accept prevention by an obstacle. As for consensus: the linguists all said that exception is extraction and speech about the remainder after the exclusion. When both aspects are established, combination between them is obligatory. So we say it is extraction and speech about the remainder by its placement, and affirmation and negation by its indication, as we will explain if Allah wills. As for rational proof, there are aspects: One: that which prevents the ruling through contradiction applies equally to part and whole, like abrogation, but it is not equal here because exception from the whole is invalid. The second: the proof of contradiction is independent by itself, like a specification proof, while exception is never independent by itself; it is only completed by what precedes it, so it is not suitable as a contradiction. However, since it is not permissible to judge by part of a sentence until it is complete, just as it is not permissible to judge by part of a word until it ends, it is possible to suspend the beginning of the speech upon its end until its end clarifies the intended meaning of its beginning. And this invalidation is the way of the opponent's school. The third: to correct what we said, and its explanation is that the existence of speech with no ruling at all, and no establishment of its ruling at all, is permissible, like prevention by contradiction by consensus, such as the divorce of a child and his manumission. The only matter is preponderance. Its explanation: when exception is made a contradiction in the ruling, the speech remains with its ruling in the beginning of the statement, then no part of the ruling remains except some of it, and that is not suitable as a ruling for all the speech at its beginning. Do you not see that 'thousand' is a proper name that does not apply to others and does not bear it: it is not permissible to call nine hundred thousand by it, unlike the specification proof; because when it contradicts the general in some part, the required ruling behind the specification proof remains established by that very thing, suitable to be established by it, like the name 'polytheists' when a type is excluded from it: the name applies to the remainder without flaw. Therefore we said that when the general is a single word or a genus noun, specification is valid down to the individual; when it is a plural form, specification ends at three, no less. Therefore it cannot be a contradiction. So it is made speech about the remainder by its reality and form, and it is a method in language that sometimes lengthens and sometimes shortens, and it is made for affirmation and negation by its indication. And its explanation is that exception is like a limit for the excepted-from. Do you not see that the first is by it? And this is because exception enters upon negation or affirmation, and affirmation ends by non-existence, and negation ends by existence. When existence is a limit for the first, or non-existence ends.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is a defense of the Hanafi position on the nature of exception (istithna) in legal and linguistic contexts. The author argues that exception does not function as a contradiction (mu'arada) that nullifies the general statement; rather, it extracts part of the statement and clarifies the intended scope. The passage begins with an example: 'There is no scholar except Zayd' affirms that Zayd is a scholar, showing that exception indicates the remainder. The author then presents the third argument: exception does not remove the speech itself from the beginning of the statement; the speech remains with its original form and ruling. Since the speech exists, it cannot be removed, but the ruling may be prevented due to a contradicting element. However, the opponent's claim that the speech itself is removed is unintelligible. Next, the Hanafi proofs are given: textual, consensus, and rational. The textual proof is the Quranic verse about Noah's stay of a thousand years minus fifty, showing that exception does not contradict the affirmation of the thousand but limits it. In reports, the ruling persists despite the exception. The consensus proof: all linguists agree that exception is extraction (istikhraj) and speech about the remainder after exclusion (thuniyya). Since both aspects are true—extraction and speech about the remainder—they must be combined: exception is extraction of the excluded part and speech about the remainder by its own linguistic placement, and it indicates affirmation or negation via its specific form. The rational proofs are three. First, any factor that prevents a ruling through contradiction (like abrogation) must apply equally to part and whole. In exception, this is not the case because exception from the whole (i.e., excepting the entire general statement) is invalid. Second, a contradictory proof is independent, like a specific text (dafil al-khusus), while exception is never independent; it depends on the preceding statement. Therefore, it cannot be a contradiction. However, because one cannot judge a partial sentence until it is complete, it is possible to suspend the beginning of the statement until its end clarifies the intended meaning. This suspension invalidates the opponent's approach. Third, the existence of speech without any ruling at all is permissible by consensus (like the speech of a child who divorces or frees a slave). The real issue is preponderance (tarjih). If exception were a contradiction, part of the ruling would remain, but that part would not be a ruling for the entire opening statement. For example, 'thousand' is a proper noun that cannot apply to nine hundred; unlike a specification (takhsis) where the general term remains applicable to the remainder without flaw. In specification, the general term remains valid for the excluded parts. Therefore, the author concludes that when the general is a single word or genus noun, specification goes down to the individual; when it is a plural, specification ends at three (minimum plural). Since exception cannot contradict, it is treated as speech about the remainder by its reality and form, and it is a linguistic tool that can vary in length. Exception functions as a limit (ghaya) for the excepted-from: it marks the endpoint of negation or affirmation. Thus, exception clarifies and limits, rather than contradicting the original statement.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithna): Linguistic device that extracts part of a statement and indicates the remainder after exclusion.
المعارضة (al-mu'arada): A proof that contradicts and nullifies the ruling of another proof.
الخصوص (al-khusus): Specification of a general term by a separate, independent proof.
الغاية (al-ghaya): A limit or endpoint that marks the boundary of a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is the nature of exception (istithna)?
A) It is a contradiction that nullifies the ruling from the excepted part.
B) It is an extraction and speech about the remainder, not a contradiction.
C) It is an independent proof that specifies the general.
D) It is a type of abrogation (naskh).

Key Takeaway
Exception clarifies the intended scope of the general statement; it is an extraction and speech about the remainder, not a contradiction.

Exception as a Limit (Ghaya) in Hanafi Usul
Explains Hanafi argument that istithna' functions as a limit, not specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi distinction between exception (istithna') as a limit (ghaya) and specification (takhsis), and apply this distinction to identify the legal effect of an exceptive phrase.

Core Idea
Exception (istithna') terminates the scope of a statement like a limit; specification leaves the general term intact for the remainder.

In Hanafi usul, exception (istithnā') is not merely a form of specification (takhsīṣ); it functions as a limit (ghāyah) that completely ends the application of the ruling for the excepted part. This passage presents the Hanafi argument distinguishing the two, using the example of the word 'alf' (thousand) and the kalima of tawhīd. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly interpreting general and exceptional statements in legal texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's view
The opponent treats exception as a counter-evidence (mu'āriḍ) that leaves part of the general term applicable. Understand why this view is rejected.
The passage calls this 'the method of the opponent's school'.
2
Analyze the Hanafi position
Exception (istithnā') acts as a limit (ghāyah) for the excepted-from statement, terminating the ruling entirely for the excepted part.
The author uses the term 'غاية' (limit/end) to describe this function.
3
Study the example of 'alf'
The word 'alf' (thousand) cannot refer to nine hundred; exception does not allow partial application, unlike specification.
Compare with 'name of polytheists' where specification leaves the name applicable to the rest.
4
Examine the kalima of tawhīd
In 'Lā ilāha illā Allāh', the exception 'illā Allāh' is an indication of affirmation while the negation is primary, illustrating the distinct function of exception.
This shows exception as an indication (ishārah) versus intentional speech (qaṣd).
5
Apply the distinction
In legal texts, when an exception follows a general command, the ruling does not apply to the excepted part; the remaining general is not 'specified' but rather the original scope is limited by the exception.
This affects how new cases are analogized under the general rule.

والثالث: لتصحيح ما قلنا، وبيان ذلك وهو أن وجود التكلم ولا حكم : له أصلاً، ولا انعقادَ له بحكمه أصلاً سائغ، مثل الامتناع بالمعارض ،بالإجماع مثل طلاق الصبي ،وإعتاقه، وإنما الشأن في الترجيح.

ولهذا قلنا إن العام إذا كان كلمة فرد، أو اسم جنس: صح إلى أن ينتهي بالفرد، وإذا كانت صيغة جمع: انتهى الخصوص إلى الثلاثة، لا غير، فلذلك بطل أن يكون معارضاً، فجعل تكلُّماً بالباقي بحقيقته وصيغته، وكان طريقاً في اللغة يطول مرةً، ويقصر أخرى، وجعل للإيجاب والنفي بإشارته.
وبيانه أن الاستثناء بمنزلة الغاية للمستثنى منه، ألا يُرى أن الأول به وهذا لأن الاستثناء يدخل على نفي أو إثبات والإثبات بالعدم ينتهي، والعدم بالوجود ينتهي، وإذا كان الوجود غايةً للأول، أو العدمُ غاية : لم يكن بد من إثبات الغاية؛ لتناهي الأول.
وهذا ثابتٌ لغةً، فكان مثل صدر الكلام، إلا أن الأول ثابت قصداً، وهذا لا، فكان إشارةً، ولذلك اختير في التوحيد : لا إله إلا الله ; ليكون الإثبات إشارةً، والنفي قصداً؛ لأن الأصل في التوحيد: تصديق القلب، فاختير في البيان الإشارة إليه، والله أعلم.
By some of the word until it ends: it is possible for the beginning of the speech to be suspended until the end so that the intended meaning of the beginning is clarified by its end, and this invalidation is the method of the opponent's school. And third: to correct what we said, and its explanation is that the existence of speech without any ruling, and no establishment of its ruling at all, is permissible, like impossibility by opposition by consensus such as the divorce of a minor and his manumission; the matter is only in preference. Its explanation: that when exception is made an opponent in the ruling, the speech with its ruling remains in the beginning of the utterance, then nothing remains of the ruling except some of it, and that is not suitable as a ruling for the entire beginning of the utterance. Do you not see that 'alf' (thousand) is a proper noun that does not apply to others, and cannot bear it; it is not permissible to call nine hundred thousand 'alf', unlike the proof of specification; because when it opposes the general in some, the sought-after ruling behind the proof of specification remains established in that very same thing, suitable to be established by it, like the name 'polytheists' if a type is specified from it, the name applies to the rest without defect. Hence we said that if the general is a single word or a generic noun, specification extends to the individual; if it is a plural form, specification ends at three, not more. Therefore it is invalid for it to be an opponent; so it is made speech with the remainder in its reality and form, and it is a path in the language that lengthens at times and shortens at others, and it is made for affirmation and negation by its indication. Its explanation: that exception is like the limit for the excepted-from, do you not see that the beginning ends with it? And this is because exception enters upon negation or affirmation: affirmation ends with non-existence, and non-existence ends with existence. If existence is the limit for the beginning, or non-existence is the limit, there must be the establishment of the limit for the termination of the beginning. This is linguistically established, so it is like the beginning of the speech, except that the beginning is established intentionally, while this is not, so it is an indication. Therefore, in tawhid, 'La ilaha illa Allah' was chosen so that affirmation is an indication and negation is intentional; because the basis of tawhid is the heart's affirmation, so in expression, indication to it was chosen. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on how exception (istithna') operates linguistically and legally, distinguishing it from specification (takhsis). The author is refuting the opponent's view that exception is a form of counter-evidence (mu'arid) that leaves the general term partially applicable. Instead, Hanafis argue that exception functions as a limit (ghaya) for the excepted-from statement, fundamentally altering its scope. The Arabic word 'alf' (one thousand) is used as an example: it cannot refer to any number less than a thousand, unlike specification which can leave the general term applicable to the remainder. The passage explains that exception enters upon either affirmation or negation and marks the endpoint of the ruling. In the kalima of tawhid, the exception 'illa Allah' serves as an indication of affirmation, while the negation is the primary intentional element, reflecting the heart's affirmation. This linguistic analysis supports the Hanafi usul principle that exception is not a simple specification but a distinct operation.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): A linguistic device that removes a part from a statement, functioning as a limit (ghaya) for the excepted-from.
الغاية (al-ghāyah): The endpoint that terminates the scope of a preceding statement, established by exception.
دليل الخصوص (dalīl al-khuṣūṣ): A proof that specifies a general term, leaving the general applicable to the remainder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how does exception (istithna') differ from specification (takhsis)?
A) Exception leaves the general term applicable to the remainder; specification does not.
B) Exception functions as a limit (ghaya) terminating the rule; specification leaves the general term applicable to the remainder.
C) Exception is only used in negative statements; specification in affirmative.
D) Exception is a counter-evidence; specification is not.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, exception (istithna') is a limit (ghaya) that terminates the rule for the excepted part, distinct from specification which leaves the general term applicable to the remainder.

Connected and Disconnected Exception in Hanafi Usul
Defines muttasil (connected) and munqati' (disconnected) exception with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between connected and disconnected exceptions by analyzing whether the excepted part can be extracted from the first statement, and identify Quranic and hadith examples of each type.

Core Idea
Connected exception extracts the excepted part; disconnected exception begins anew — a subtle linguistic shift with major interpretive consequences.

In Hanafi usul, understanding the structure of exception (istithna') is crucial for correctly interpreting legal texts. This passage defines the two primary types: muttasil (connected) and munqati' (disconnected). A connected exception allows the excepted term to be logically extracted from the first statement, while a disconnected exception requires treating the excepted phrase as a new beginning, often meaning 'but' or 'however.' This distinction determines how we understand Quranic verses and hadiths containing exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the two categories
Understand that exception is divided into muttasil (connected) and munqati' (disconnected). Muttasil is the original type where the excepted part can be extracted from the first statement.
This is a foundational taxonomy in Hanafi usul.
2
Define connected exception
In muttasil, the excepted part is genuinely part of the first statement and can be extracted. Example: 'The students came except Zaid' – Zaid is a student who did not come.
3
Define disconnected exception
In munqati', the excepted part is not part of the first statement. It cannot be extracted; instead, it is a metaphorical new beginning, often translated as 'but.' Example from Quran: 'Indeed, they are an enemy to me, except the Lord of the worlds' – the Lord is not an enemy, so it means 'but the Lord of the worlds.'
4
Identify the Quranic and hadith examples
The passage lists examples: Shu'ara 26:77 (munqati'), Waqi'ah 56:25-26 (munqati'), Baqarah 2:160 (munqati'), Baqarah 2:237 (istithna' hal), and a hadith about retaliation (istithna' hal). Understand why each is classified as disconnected.
The hadith 'except equal for equal' is an exception of state, a subtype of disconnected exception.
5
Apply the distinction
When encountering an exception in a text, first check if the excepted item could logically be part of the first statement. If yes, it is muttasil; if no, it is munqati'. This affects the legal meaning.
For example, in Baqarah 2:160, the repenters cannot be part of the transgressors, so it is munqati' meaning 'unless they repent.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوٌّ لِي إِلَّا رَبَّ الْعَلَمِينَ ) الشعراء /۷۷: أي لكن رب العالمين.

وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا أَن يَعْفُونَ ) البقرة/ ۲۳۷ : استثناء حال.

وكذلك قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : (إلا) سواء بسواء»: استثناء حال،
Exception is of two types: connected and disconnected. As for the connected, it is the original, and its interpretation is what we mentioned. As for the disconnected, it is what cannot be extracted from the first (statement) because the beginning did not include it, so it is made a metaphorical new beginning. Allah Most High said: 'Indeed, they are an enemy to me, except the Lord of the worlds' (Shu'ara 26:77) meaning 'but the Lord of the worlds'. Similarly: 'They will not hear therein any idle talk or sin except a saying: Peace, peace' (Waqi'ah 56:25-26). And His saying 'Except those who repent' (Baqarah 2:160) is a disconnected exception because the repenters are not included in the beginning of the statement, so its meaning is 'unless they repent', and the beginning is carried upon the generality of conditions by the indication of the exception; as if He said: 'And those, they are the transgressors in every condition except the condition of repentance.' Similarly His saying 'Unless they (the women) forgive' (Baqarah 2:237) is an exception of state. Similarly the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'except equal for equal' is an exception of state.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage defines the two types of exception (istithna') in Hanafi usul. Connected exception (muttasil) is the primary type where the excepted part is genuinely part of the preceding statement and can be extracted from it; for example, 'The students came except Zaid.' Disconnected exception (munqati') occurs when the excepted part is not included in the preceding statement; it is interpreted metaphorically as a new beginning, often meaning 'but' or 'however'. The Quranic examples illustrate: in Shu'ara 26:77, 'except the Lord of the worlds' is disconnected because 'the Lord' was not included among the enemies. Similarly, Surah Waqi'ah mentions hearing no idle talk except peaceful greetings, again disconnected. In Baqarah 2:160, 'except those who repent' is disconnected because the repenters were not part of the original description. Baqarah 2:237 mentions an exception of state (istithna' hal) regarding women forgiving a portion of dower. The hadith about retaliation 'equal for equal' is also classified as an exception of state. Understanding these types helps correctly interpret Quranic and legal texts where exception appears.

Key Terms
متصل (muttasil): Connected exception: the excepted part is genuinely part of the excepted-from statement.
منقطع (munqati'): Disconnected exception: the excepted part is not part of the excepted-from statement; interpreted as 'but'.
استثناء حال (istithnā' ḥāl): An exception that indicates a specific state or condition, as in 'except when they forgive'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the key difference between connected (muttasil) and disconnected (munqati') exception?
A) Connected exception is used only in the Quran; disconnected is used only in Hadith.
B) Connected exception allows the excepted part to be extracted from the first statement; disconnected does not.
C) Disconnected exception always means 'except'; connected means 'but'.
D) There is no difference; both are the same.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between connected and disconnected exception hinges on whether the excepted part can be extracted from the first statement; disconnected exceptions require interpreting 'illa' as 'but' or 'unless'.

Connected and Disconnected Exception (Istithna') and Exception of Measured Items
Defines istithna' types and analyzes a Hanafi internal ikhtilaf on muqaddarat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between connected (muttasil) and disconnected (munqati') exception in Hanafi usul, and apply the rule on exception of measured items (muqaddarat) from a different genus.

Core Idea
In Hanafi usul, disconnected exception does not extract from the general term; measured items are one genus in meaning for valid exception.

This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi introduces the two fundamental types of exception (istithna') and then delves into a key Hanafi internal disagreement over whether an exception of a measured item from a different genus is valid. Understanding this distinction is crucial for parsing legal language correctly—whether in Quranic verses or contractual statements. We will walk through the definitions, Quranic examples, and the reasoning of the Hanafi masters.

Guided Path
1
Define and distinguish muttasil and munqati'
First, understand the core definitions: muttasil is when the excepted item is part of the genus of the first part; munqati' is when it is not, and the exception is treated as a new statement. Note that muttasil is the original (asl) form.
Connected exception effectively extracts from the general term; disconnected does not.
2
Analyze Quranic examples of munqati'
Read the verses cited (26:77, 56:25-26, 2:160) and see how the exception is interpreted as 'but' or 'unless', showing it does not extract from the preceding general statement. Understand the linguistic basis for this classification.
The exception of 'Rabb al-'Alamin' from 'they' is disconnected because Allah is not of the genus of idols.
3
Understand the agreed case: exception of non-measured item
When someone says 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except a garment,' all Hanafi jurists agree this is disconnected and invalid; the garment is not deducted. Grasp why extraction is not valid: the garment is not of the same genus as dirhams in form or meaning.
This is the baseline ruling.
4
Examine the Hanafi ikhtilaf on muqaddarat
When the excepted item is a measured item (muqaddar) like cloth, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule the exception valid because muqaddarat share a common meaning as prices. Muhammad holds it invalid. Trace each imam's dalil and response.
The key is whether exception operates on meaning (ma'na) or form (surah).
5
Apply the principle to the 'deposit' example
Read how the same principle applies to a statement like 'I owe you a thousand dirhams as a deposit.' This is a connected exception because it is a modifying explanation within the same genus, changing the reality but remaining valid.
This shows the flexibility of the usul rule across scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غاية : لم يكن بد من إثبات الغاية؛ لتناهي الأول.
وهذا ثابتٌ لغةً، فكان مثل صدر الكلام، إلا أن الأول ثابت قصداً، وهذا لا، فكان إشارةً، ولذلك اختير في التوحيد : لا إله إلا الله ؛ ليكون الإثبات إشارةً، والنفي قصداً؛ لأن الأصل في التوحيد: تصديق القلب، فاختير في البيان الإشارة إليه، والله أعلم.
[ أنواع الاستثناء : ]
والاستثناء نوعان : متصل، ومنقطع.
أما المتصل : فهو الأصل، وتفسيره ما ذكرنا.
وأما المنقطع: فما لا يصح استخراجه من الأول؛ لأن الصدر لم يتناوله، فجعل مبتدأ مجازاً.
قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنَّهُمْ عَدُوٌّ لِي إِلَّا رَبَّ الْعَلَمِينَ﴾ [الشعراء:77] أي: لكن رب العالمين.
وكذلك: ﴿وَلَا يَسْمَعُونَ فِيهَا لَغْوًا وَلَا تَأْثِيمًا إِلَّا قِيلًا سَلَامًا سَلَامًا﴾ [الواقعة:25-26].
وقوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا الَّذِينَ تَابُوا﴾ [البقرة:160] استثناء منقطع؛ لأن التائبين غير داخلين في صدر الكلام فكان معناه إلا أن يتوبوا، ويُحمل الصدر على عموم الأحوال؛ بدلالة الثنيا، فكأنه قال: وأولئك هم الفاسقون بكل حال إلا حال التوبة.
وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْفُونَ﴾ [البقرة:237] استثناء حال.
وكذلك قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إلا سواء بسواء» استثناء حال،
فيكون الصدر عاماً في الأحوال، وذلك لا يصلح إلا في المقدر.
واتفق أصحابنا رحمهم الله أن قول الرجل: لفلان عليَّ ألف درهم إلا ثوباً أن هذا استثناء منقطع؛ لأن استخراجه لا يصلح، فجعل نفياً مبتدأ، ونفيه لا يؤثر في الألف.
وأما إذا استثنى المقدَّر من خلاف جنسه فقد قال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله: هو صحيح.
وقال محمد رحمه الله: ليس بصحيح؛ لما قلنا من الأصل، وجعل استثناء منقطعاً، فلم ينقص من الألف شيء.
وقال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله: هو صحيح؛ لأن المقدرات جنس واحد في المعنى؛ لأنها تصلح ثمناً، ولكن الصور مختلفة، فصح الاستثناء في المعنى. وقد قلنا: إن الاستثناء تكلَّم بالباقي بعد الثَّنْيا معنى، لا صورةً، فإذا صح الاستخراج من طريق المعنى بقي المعنى في القدر المستثنى تسمية الدراهم بلا معنى، وذلك هو معنى حقيقة الاستثناء، فلذلك بطل قدره من الأول، بخلاف ما ليس بمقدر من الأموال؛ لأن المعنى مختلف، فلم يصح استخراجه.
وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا فيمن قال لفلان عليَّ ألف درهم وديعةً: إنه يصح موصولاً، لأنه بيان مغيّر؛ لأن الدراهم تصلح أن تكون عليه حفظاً، إلا أنه تغيير للحقيقة، فيصح موصولاً.
وكذلك رجل قال: أسلمت إلى عشرة دراهم في كذا، لكني لم
Purpose: there had to be proof of the end/limit (ghayah); because the first part ends. And this is established linguistically, so it is similar to the beginning of speech, except that the first part is established intentionally, and this is not, so it is a reference. Therefore, in tawhid, 'La ilaha illa Allah' was chosen so that affirmation is implied and negation is intended, because the basis of tawhid is belief of the heart, so in expression, reference to it was chosen. And Allah knows best. [Types of Exception:] Exception is of two types: connected and disconnected. As for connected: it is the original, and its explanation is what we mentioned. As for disconnected: it is what cannot be validly extracted from the first part, because the first part did not include it, so it is treated as a new beginning metaphorically. Allah Most High said: 'Indeed, they are an enemy to me, except the Lord of the worlds' (26:77), meaning: but the Lord of the worlds. Similarly: 'And they will not hear therein any idle talk or sin, except the saying: Peace, peace.' (56:25-26). And His saying: 'Except those who repent' (2:160) is a disconnected exception, because those who repent are not included in the first part of the speech, so its meaning is 'unless they repent', and the first part is interpreted as general regarding states, by the indication of the exception, as if He said: 'Those are the transgressors in every state except the state of repentance.' Similarly His saying: 'Except that they (the women) forgive' (2:237) is an exception of state. Similarly the Prophet's saying: 'except equal for equal' is an exception of state, so the first part is general regarding states, and that is only valid for measured (muqaddar) items. Our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) agreed that when a man says: 'I owe someone a thousand dirhams except a garment,' this is a disconnected exception, because its extraction is not valid, so it is treated as a negation at the beginning, and its negation does not affect the thousand. But if one makes an exception of a measured item from a different genus, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said: it is valid. Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it is not valid, due to the principle we stated, and it is made a disconnected exception, so nothing is deducted from the thousand. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf said: it is valid, because measured items are one genus in meaning, since they can serve as prices, but the forms differ, so the exception is valid in meaning. We have said that exception speaks of the remainder after excluding in meaning, not in form. So if extraction is valid from the perspective of meaning, the meaning remains in the extracted amount, calling them dirhams without meaning, and that is the essence of exception. Therefore, its amount is annulled from the first, unlike non-measured items of wealth, because the meaning differs, so its extraction is not valid. Based on this principle, we say about someone who says: 'I owe someone a thousand dirhams as a deposit' that it is valid as a connected exception, because it is a modifying explanation, since dirhams can be held as a trust, but it is a change of reality, so it is valid as connected. Similarly, a man said: 'I paid in advance ten dirhams for such-and-such, but I did not...'
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Bazdawi defines the two types of exception (istithna') — connected (mutttasil) and disconnected (munqati') — and then addresses a specific Hanafi internal dispute regarding the exception of measured items (muqaddarat) from a different genus. The author begins with a note on the concept of 'ghayah' (limit/end) as a precursor, emphasizing its linguistic basis and its use in expressions like 'la ilaha illa Allah' to combine negation and affirmation. He then states that exception is of two types: connected, where the extracted item is part of the genus of the first part, and disconnected, where it is not. Examples from the Quran illustrate disconnected exception: the verse 'except the Lord of the worlds' is interpreted as 'but the Lord of the worlds', and 'except those who repent' is understood as 'unless they repent', showing that the exception does not extract from the preceding general statement but rather specifies a different situation. The author notes that connected exception is the original (asl), and disconnected is treated as a new beginning. The passage then moves to a key Hanafi ikhtilaf: when a person says 'I owe you a thousand dirhams except a garment', the jurists agree this is disconnected and invalid (the garment is not deducted). However, if the exception is of a measured item (e.g., 'except a piece of cloth' from 'a thousand dirhams'), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule the exception valid because all measured items (muqaddarat) share a common meaning as potential prices, even though their forms differ. Imam Muhammad disagrees, insisting on the literal form; for him, the exception is disconnected and does not reduce the thousand. The author also applies the same principle to the phrase 'a thousand dirhams as a deposit', ruling it a valid connected exception because the explanation modifies the reality but remains within the same genus. The text ends abruptly with a case of salam (advance payment). Throughout, the commentary follows the author's order, clarifying each ruling and its basis.

Key Terms
الاستثناء المتصل (al-istithna' al-muttasil): Exception where the extracted item is part of the genus of the first part and can be validly extracted from it.
الاستثناء المنقطع (al-istithna' al-munqati'): Exception where the extracted item is not part of the genus of the first part and cannot be validly extracted; treated as a new beginning metaphorically.
المقدر (al-muqaddar): Measured or quantified items that can serve as prices or equivalents, such as dirhams, dinars, and cloth (by measure).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is a disconnected exception, but still deducts the cloth's value.
C) It is a disconnected exception, and nothing is deducted.
D) It is invalid as an exception, so the debt becomes ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the validity of an exception (istithna') depends on whether the extracted item is from the same genus in form or meaning; measured items (muqaddarat) share a common meaning as prices, allowing valid exception across genera according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Exception of a Quantified Thing from a Different Genus
Dispute on istithna of muqaddar from different genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi dispute on istithna of a quantified thing from a different genus and apply the rule to debt scenarios.

Core Idea
Quantified items are one genus in meaning, allowing valid exception across forms.

This passage presents a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school. While the general rule is that an exception from a different genus is invalid (istithna munqati), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf carve out an exception for quantified items (muqaddarat) due to their functional unity as prices. Understanding this helps us appreciate how meaning can override form in usul reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The issue is whether an exception (istithna) of a quantified item (e.g., cloth) from a debt of dirhams is valid when the excepted item is from a different genus.
The key phrase is 'quantified thing from a different genus'.
2
State the Two Positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: valid. Muhammad: invalid.
Both positions are within the Hanafi school; this is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze Muhammad's Argument
Muhammad applies the general rule: since the genus differs, the exception is disconnected (munqati), so nothing is deducted.
His dalil is the principle that exception requires same genus.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's Argument
They argue that quantified items (muqaddarat) are one genus in meaning because they serve as prices, so the exception is valid in meaning, not form.
They prioritize meaning over literal form.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical difference: if someone says 'I owe you 1000 dirhams except a cloth', Muhammad says he still owes 1000; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say he owes 1000 minus the cloth's value.
This shows the real-world impact of the usul dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إذا استثنى المقدَّر من خلاف جنسه فقد قال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله : هو صحيح. وقال محمد رحمه الله : ليس بصحيح؛ لما قلنا من الأصل، وجعل استثناء منقطعاً، فلم ينقص من الألف شيء. وقال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله : هو صحيح؛ لأن المقدرات جنس واحد في المعنى ؛ لأنها تصلح ثمناً ، ولكن الصور مختلفة، فصح الاستثناء في المعنى. وقد قلنا: إن الاستثناء تكلَّم بالباقي بعد الثَّنْيا معنى، لا صورةً، فإذا صح الاستخراج من طريق المعنى بقي المعنى في القدر المستثنى تسمية الدراهم بلا معنى، وذلك هو معنى حقيقة الاستثناء، فلذلك بطل قدره من الأول، بخلاف ما ليس بمقدر من الأموال؛ لأن المعنى مختلف، فلم يصح استخراجه.
As for if one excepts a quantified thing from a different genus, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said: it is valid. And Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it is not valid, due to what we said from the principle, and he considered it a disconnected exception (istithna munqati‘), so nothing is deducted from the thousand. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them) said: it is valid because quantified things are of one genus in meaning, as they are fit for being a price, but their forms differ, so the exception is valid in meaning. And we have said: the exception speaks of the remainder after the exclusion in meaning, not in form. So if the extraction is valid from the path of meaning, the meaning remains in the excepted amount by naming dirhams without meaning, and that is the reality of exception, therefore its amount is void from the first, unlike that which is not quantified among properties, because the meaning differs, so its extraction is not valid.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute among the Hanafi founders regarding the validity of an exception (istithna) when the excepted item is quantified (muqaddar) but from a different genus than the principal item. The example: someone says 'I owe so-and-so one thousand dirhams except a cloth.' Dirhams are quantified, cloth is not. Muhammad al-Shaybani rules the exception invalid (mursal/munqati‘), meaning nothing is deducted from the thousand. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule it valid because all quantified items (like dirhams, dinars, measures) are considered one genus in meaning—they serve as prices—so the exception is valid in meaning, even if not in form. They hold that the reality of exception is to speak of the remainder after exclusion in meaning, not in form. Therefore, the excepted amount (the value of the cloth) is void from the total, reducing the debt accordingly. This is contrasted with non-quantified properties (like animals or goods) where meaning differs, so exception across genera is invalid. The arguments are based on the nature of quantified items as homogenous in function as mediums of exchange.

Key Terms
استثناء منقطع (istithnā’ munqaṭi‘): An exception where the excepted item is not of the same genus as the principal, making the exception grammatically disconnected. In Hanafi usul, it is usually invalid unless the excepted item is quantified.
مقدّر (muqaddar): A quantified thing, such as a specific measure, weight, or number of coins, that can serve as a price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because all quantified items are considered one genus in meaning as they serve as prices.
C) Because the debtor intended to give a gift.
D) Because Muhammad also agreed.

Key Takeaway
The validity of an exception of a quantified thing from a different genus depends on whether we prioritize meaning over form; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf do, Muhammad does not.

Modifying Explanations (Bayan Mughayyir) in Acknowledgments of Deposit
Ruling on the validity of a connected statement modifying a debt acknowledgment into a deposit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule regarding modifying explanations (bayan mughayyir) to determine the validity of a connected statement that changes a debt acknowledgment into a deposit.

Core Idea
A modifying explanation that changes the legal reality is valid only if connected to the original statement.

This passage applies a key usul al-fiqh principle – bayan mughayyir – to the fiqh of acknowledgments (iqrar). Understanding this rule helps distinguish between a valid modification and a retraction. We will examine how the Hanafi school treats a claim of deposit made in the same breath as a debt acknowledgment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement and its components
Break down the phrase: 'I owe so-and-so a thousand dirhams as a deposit.' Note the initial acknowledgment of debt (''alayya alf dirham') and the modifying phrase ('wadi‘atan').
The word 'wadi‘a' is the modifier.
2
Recognize the modifying effect
Understand that 'wadi‘a' changes the legal nature from a liability (debt) to a trust (amanah). This is a 'bayan mughayyir' because it alters the reality of the statement.
Dirhams can be held as trust, so the modification is possible in genus.
3
Apply the condition of connection (ittisal)
According to Hanafi usul, a bayan mughayyir is valid only if it is connected (mawsul) to the original statement – said in one breath without pause. If disconnected, it would be a retraction.
Connection preserves the unity of the statement.
4
Derive the ruling
If the statement is connected, the acknowledgment is valid as a deposit (wadi‘a) with the claimed non-delivery. If disconnected, the modification is invalid and the original debt stands.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى هذا الأصل قلنا فيمن قال لفلان عليَّ ألف درهم وديعةً : إنه يصح موصولاً، لأنه بيان مغيّر ؛ لأن الدراهم تصلح أن تكون عليه حفظاً، إلا أنه تغيير للحقيقة، فيصح موصولاً.
And on this principle we said regarding one who says: 'So-and-so has a thousand dirhams against me as a deposit (wadi‘a):' It is valid connected (mawsulan), because it is a modifying explanation (bayan mughayyir); because dirhams can be upon him as a trust (hifz), but it is a change of reality, so it is valid connected.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage applies the previously discussed principle of 'bayan mughayyir' (modifying explanation) to the case of an acknowledgment (iqrar) of a debt claimed to be a deposit (wadi‘a) but with a denial of receipt. The ruling: If someone says 'I owe so-and-so a thousand dirhams as a deposit' (meaning they were entrusted to him but he claims he never received them), this acknowledgment is valid only if the statement is connected (mawsul) – i.e., he says the entire phrase in one breath without pause. The reason: The word 'wadi‘a' modifies the reality of the debt (which is normally a liability) into a trust relationship. Dirhams can indeed be held as a trust (amanah), so the modifier is possible. However, because it changes the essential nature (from debt to trust), it requires connection to avoid being a retraction. The Hanafi school accepts this as a valid modifying explanation.

Key Terms
بيان مغيّر (bayān mughayyir): A statement that modifies the legal reality of a previous statement, akin to an exception but changing the genus or nature.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right or liability.
موصولاً (mawsulan): Connected; uttered in one breath without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it is a modifying explanation that changes the reality of the statement.
C) Because the dirhams are not fit for deposit.
D) Because it is considered a separate acknowledgment.

Key Takeaway
A modifying explanation (bayan mughayyir) that changes the legal nature of a statement is valid only when connected to the original statement.

Claiming Defective Dirhams: Generality vs Accidental Qualities
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specifying defective dirhams after acknowledgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of 'amm (generality) to distinguish between a valid specification of a subtype and an invalid retraction in acknowledgments.

Core Idea
The dispute over defective dirhams hinges on whether defectiveness is a subtype (valid) or an accidental defect (retraction).

This lesson examines a classical intra-Hanafi dispute about acknowledgments. When someone acknowledges a debt of dirhams and immediately adds that they are defective (ziyuf), is that claim valid? The answer depends on how we interpret the general term 'dirham' and whether 'defective' is a subtype or an accidental quality. This case illuminates key usul concepts: 'amm (generality), takhsīs (specification), haqiqah vs majaz, and the distinction between essential and accidental attributes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Positions
State the factual scenario: a person acknowledges dirhams as a loan or sale price, then claims they are defective (ziyuf). Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad accept this if claimed immediately (connected), while Abu Hanifa rejects it entirely.
Connection (ittiṣāl) is key for the Ṣāḥibayn.
2
Analyze the Usul Reasoning of the Ṣāḥibayn
Examine their argument: the word 'dirham' is a general term encompassing both good and defective types. Since good dirhams are predominant, specifying defective is like using a metaphorical expression (majāz) to indicate a subtype, which is valid when connected.
They treat 'defective' as a takhsīṣ (specification) of the general term.
3
Analyze the Usul Reasoning of Abu Hanifa
Understand Abu Hanifa's counterargument: defectiveness (ziyāfa) is an accidental quality (ʿāriḍ) and a defect (ʿayb), not a subtype inherent to the meaning of 'dirham'. The absolute name does not bear such a quality, so claiming it constitutes a retraction (rujūʿ) of the entire acknowledgment.
He analogizes to claiming a term or option, which similarly are not part of the original obligation.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Articulate the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the acknowledger must pay good dirhams; under the Ṣāḥibayn, he pays defective dirhams if the claim is connected and proven.
No explicit tarjīḥ is given, but the Ṣāḥibayn's reasoning is more detailed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا أقرَّ بالدراهم قرضاً، أو ثمن بيع، وقال: هي زيوف: صح عندهما موصولاً ؛ لأن الدراهم نوعان: جياد، وزيوف، إلا أن الجياد غالبةٌ، فصار الآخرُ كالمجاز، فصح التغيير إليه موصولاً. وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله : لا يُقبل وإن وصل؛ لأن الزيافة عارضةٌ وعيب؛ لأنه غِش، فلا يحتمله مطلق الاسم، بل يكون رجوعاً، كدعوى الأجل في الدين، ودعوى الخيار في البيع.
And if he acknowledges dirhams as a loan or as the price of a sale, and says: 'They are defective (ziyuf),' it is valid according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if connected, because dirhams are of two types: good and defective, but the good are predominant, so the other becomes like metaphor (majaz), so the change to it is valid if connected. And Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it is not accepted even if connected, because defectiveness (ziyafa) is accidental and a defect, as it is adulteration (ghish), so the absolute name does not bear it, but it is a retraction, like the claim of a term in a debt, and the claim of an option in a sale.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage discusses a case where someone acknowledges a debt of dirhams (as a loan or sale price) and then claims that the dirhams are defective (ziyuf, i.e., counterfeit or of low quality). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, if the claim is made connected (in the same breath), it is valid because the word 'dirham' encompasses both good and defective types, although good dirhams are the norm. Thus, specifying 'defective' is a metaphorical usage that modifies the previous statement, and connection makes it acceptable. Abu Hanifa, however, rejects this even if connected, because defectiveness is an accidental quality (not inherent) and constitutes a defect (adulteration). The absolute term 'dirham' does not accommodate such a specification; it amounts to a retraction (ruju‘) of the acknowledgment. He analogizes it to claiming a term (e.g., that the debt was due later) or an option (khiyar) in a sale, which would not be accepted because they change the nature of the obligation.

Key Terms
زيوف (ziyūf): Defective dirhams that are of low quality or counterfeit, containing adulteration (ghish).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the person is lying.
B) Because defectiveness is not a subtype but an accidental defect, making the claim a retraction.
C) Because the connection is not proper.
D) Because Muhammad did not accept it.

Key Takeaway
The validity of specifying a quality after an acknowledgment depends on whether the quality is a subtype (valid) or an accidental defect (retraction) in Hanafi usul.
